CHONGOING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
A.    PROJECT BACKGROUND
With the national economic and social development of Chongqifg municipality, the municipal
people's government of Chongqing has fully realized the importance of increasing the ratio of
urbanization and speeding up the construction of urban infrastructure and improvement of the
environment. In order to spur the development of national economy in Chongqing in a sustainable
manner, increase the economic growth rate, improve the living environment of the people and
enlarge the extent to which the various groups of the whole society can benefit from the
improvement, the people's government of Chongqing municipality has selected a series of specific
environment improvement and infrastructure construction projects in a number of districts, cities
and counties within its territory and has input a huge amount of funds to them. In 2001, the
municipal government obtained a loan of US$200 million from the World Bank for urban
environment construction in a move to perfect Chongqing's infrastructure function and social
livelihood facilities in urban and rural townships and promote the urbanization process. For the
reasons of reduced number of subprojects and reduced volume of works, changes in the source of
funds and smaller amount of bidding funds than the investment budget, there will be a US$60 to 70
million saving of the World Bank loan and the municipal government has decided to continue.using
this saved sum of money for constructing environment facilities and infrastructure in Chongqing.
Chongqing Urban Environment Saving Loan Project consists of five environment improvement
projects and three water supply projects. They are: Comprehensive environment improvement of
Bachuan and Huaiyuan Rivers in Tongliang County; Comprehensive environment improvement of
Laixi River (Longshui section) in Dazu County; Comprehensive environment improvement of
Taohuaxi River (Longshui section) in Changshou District; Urban Water Supply Project in Bishan
County; Comprehensive Environment Improvement Project of Binan River in Bishan County;
Comprehensive Riverside Environment Improvement Project in Wulong County; Water supply
project in Shuangfu Township, Ji.angjin City and Water Supply Project in Dongyang Township,
Beibei District. The locations of these eight projects are as shown in Fig. 1.
The construction of these sewage treatment plants is helpful to mitigate the burden of pollution
caused by sewage, improve the ecological environment, and improve the residents' living
conditions and quality, while the construction of these water plants is helpful to solve the problem of
water supply for industrial production and domestic livelihood. The construction of these
comprehensive environment improvement projects is helpful to improve not only the flood-
containing capability of the riverbanks and protect the riverside area from flood, but also improve
the urban road transportation, urban natural environment and living environment as well as the
overall functions of the city. Generally speaking, these projects are helpful to beautify the city,
improve the environment for tourism and investment, spur the economic development in the
involved districts, counties and cities and quicken the urbanization process.
The construction of these projects will bring about direct benefit to 1.5 million people living in an
area of 1,329 square kilometers. The success of these projects will promote the sustainable
development of society and economy in the project area
These projects will be constructed in a period of 24 months from October 2004 to October 2006.

B.        IMPACTS OF THE PROJECTS
By land acquisition (or occupation) and house demolition, this project will permanently acquire land
of 1595.8mu, demolish house areas of 42514.2M2, affecting 46 villages in 8 rural townships of 7
counties (cities or districts) totaling 4,525 people in 1,146 households, of which 420 people in 122
households will be affected both by land acquisition and house demolition. As the land taken by the
urban environment projects is mostly shaped             in narrow   strips, the impact of land acquisition        is
limited with an average impact rate of 3% and the highest impact rate is only 32%. In addition,
according to the socioeconomic survey, the major income of the resettled people comes mainly
from non-agricultural sources. Therefore, land acquisition will not cause a major impact on the
resettled persons' income form agricultural production. See Table 1 for a list of affected population,
households, institutes, enterprises, and shops.

In addition, the people affected by these projects include 124 people of the vulnerable

C.     POLICIES ON RESETTLEMENT COMPENSATION
The policies applied to the resettlement for these projects are based on the Land Administration
Law of the PRC, Regulations on Land Administration in Provisions for Urban Residence Demolition
and Relocation in Chongqing Municipality (issued in Ordinance No. 53 by Chongqing Municipal
People's Government on March 1999) and Measures for Compensation for Land Acquisition in
Chongqing (issued in Ordinance No. 55 by Chongqing Municipal People's Government on
September 1999) laws and regulations promulgated by the  local district, county or city
governments and World Bank policies regarding involuntary resettlement.
The major policy principles are:
1) Measures are acquired to reduce the negative impact of resettlement to a minimum;
2) Compensation and resettlement plans made can improve the resettled persons' living
standards or at least restore them to the previous level;
3) The resettled persons are adequately consulted to give them chance to fully participate in the
making and implementation of the resettlement plan;
4) All the affected properties are compensated for at the replacement cost;
5) The displace persons are paid all the compensation for the losses before land acquisition and
house demolition.
The following polices are to be implemented:
(1) Compensation for permanent acquisition of land
When the rural collective-owned land is acquired, all the losses shall be reasonably compensated.
The compensation for acquiring farmland shall include the land compensation, resettlement
subsidy and compensation for ground attachments and crops. In the case of acquiring farmland,
land and resettlement compensation shall be paid at the rate of 10 to 30 times as much as the
average annual yield of the farmland in the past three years; in the case of acquiring garden land,
the land and resettlement compensation shall be paid at the rate of 1.2 times as much as the
compensation rate for farmland; in the case of acquiring ftshponds, the land and resettlement
compensation shall be paid at the rate of 1.3 times as much as the compensation rate for farmiand
in the case of acquiring non-farmland, the land compensation and resettlement subsidy shall be
paid at the rate of 1/2 of the rate of compensation for farmland; in the case of acquiring state-
owned riverside.shallow land, compensation is made for the crops on it only. In the case of
acquiring enterprise or institution's land, compensation shall be made at the evaluated land price.
See Table 4 for the rate of compensation for permanent acquisition of land.

(2) Policies regarding compensation for temporary land occupation
Compensation for temporary land occupation shall be made in the following manner: one growing
season's crop compensation is made if the temporary land occupation lasts less than one growing
season, or 2.5 growing seasons' crop compensation is made if the temporary land occupation lasts
for one year or one year's yield of land is paid if the temporary land occupation lasts for half a year.
The compensation shall be paid directly to the farmers and shall be not less than the loss incurred
to the farmers. The re-cultivation of land temporally taken shall be the responsibility of the project
construction unit and the re-cultivated land is handed over to the affected persons after an
acceptance inspection by the village leadership.

(3) Policies regarding compensation for urban residential houses demolition
The urban residents' families shall receive house demolition compensation at the estimated market
price (including land price), which shall be equivalent to the replacement price. They shall at the
same time receive the compensation for demolished house attachments and transition allowance,
movement allowance and bounty. See Table 5 for a list of compensation rates implemented in the
affected localities.

(4) Policies regarding compensation for rural residential houses demolition
The rural residents' families shall receive house demolition compensation at the estimated market
price, which shall be equivalent to the replacement price. The loss of house sites shall be
compensated for at the rate of 3Dm2 per person at the actual local land price. They shall at the
same time receive the compensation for demolished house attachments and transition allowance,
movement allowance and bounty. See Table 6 for a list of compensation rates implemented in the
affected localities.

(5) Policies regarding compensation for affected enterprises and institutions
The affected enterprises and institutions shall receive compensation for demolished houses and
acquired land at the replacement price and at the same time receive facility compensation, financial
subsides (for loss due to discontinuation of operation) and relocation allowances. After receiving
the monetary compensation, the affected enterprise or institutions may choose to rebuild their
houses at the back of original location, at another location, renovate existing houses not used, or
not to rebuild.

CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
(6) Policies regarding compensation for affected shops
The shop owners shall receive compensations for loss of land and houses at the replacement price
and at the same time receive facility compensation, financial subsides and resettlement allowances.
After receiving the monetary compensations, they may choose to purchase shops. Temporary
discontinuation of operation of shops during construction of the project shall also be compensated
for.
(7) Compensation for affected public facilities, ground attachments and sparse trees shall be made
at the replacement price.
(8) Illegal buildings and temporary structures not demolished in time shall be compensated for at
the replacement price for buildings.
D.     HOUSE REBUILDING PLAN
The house-rebuilding plan involves 66 urban households, 122 rural households, 18 enterprises and
institutions, and 38 shops.
(1) Rehabilitation of urban and rural residential houses
These projects will cause the demolition and relocation of 11,288.9m2 of urban residences,
affecting 330 persons in 66 households and 16,283.1m2 of rural residences, affecting 420 persons
in 122 households. After receiving the compensation at the replacement price, the affected persons
may choose to purchase cheap uniformly constructed resettlement apartments, new commercial
apartments or second-hand apartments. In addition, the rural residents may choose to build their
own houses.
Those who purchase cheap resettlement houses may buy such houses at the compensation price
and at the space standard of 18 m2 (17m2 in Tongliang County) per person. For limitation of
design, the excessive space is to be purchased at a rate 50% as much as the construction cost if it
is not more than 5m2 and if the space is in excess of 5m2 but less than the space of the
demolished house, it may be purchased at the combination price (construction cost plus land price).
Any part exceeding the space of the demolished house is to be purchased at the market price of a
commercial house. The demolisher shall construct facilities such as water and ground leveling in
the resettlement area; water and power supplies shall be constructed in the resettled houses.
Those who choose monetary compensation and purchase commercial houses in the affected
localities may be exempted from the tax derived from the 18m2 (17m2 in Tongliang County) per
person space standard. For those who cannot afford to buy commercial apartments, resettlement
houses or second-hand houses, the local government shall provide cheap rent houses after they
have received the compensation.
Rural residents who choose to build their own houses by themselves shall be provided with sites
free of charge by the local government at the average per-capita space standard. They shall build
such houses according to the plan made by the village or township.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 R4 - AUGUST 2004                      PAGE 8



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Facilities such as water, power and gas supplies, transportation, communications and cable TV
systems shall be constructed in the resettlement areas and commercial residential centers.
Schools, post offices, banks, food markets, bus stops, hospitals and other facilities shall be
constructed around the residential area to convenience the residents. The resettled persons may
choose to buy apartments of different grades in the residential area at their own will. These houses
are much better than their former houses (most of which were built in the 1970s to 1 980s) in quality,
structure, environment and accessibility. The second-hand houses are mostly old houses left by
the enterprises and institutions and are also better than their former houses in location, quality and
structure. Part of the vulnerable group suffering domestic poverty shall be provided with cheap-rent
houses by the government.
(2) Affected enterprises
These projects will affect 15 enterprises, of which two are no longer in production, one operates
seasonally and one is not running well. Three enterprises are affected by land acquisition only, six
are to be completely relocated and the rest are to be partly demolished. Enterprises whose land is
acquired will receive land compensation at the estimated land price, while those to be completely
relocated may, after receiving the compensation for construction land and buildings, choose to
move into the local industrial parks or planned new urban areas. As the transportation,
supplementary facilities and environment are uniformly planned, such enterprises will have better
operating conditions than before. The'income loss of the employees of such enterprises during the
transition period will be compensated for. Enterprises to be partly demolished may choose to
rebuild their houses or use the compensation for other purposes.
(3) Affected institutions
The proposed projects will affect three institutions including two whose old offices are to be
demolished. These two institutions have new offices and will receive house compensation. The
Shuren College partly demolished will rebuild backwards.
(4) Affected shops
The projects will affect 38 shops of which 36 are to be completely demolished and relocated and 34
of them are located in Dazu County. These shops are all on the ground floor of the building of
which the second floor serves as the domestic living area. Two shops in Wulong County will not be
demolished and only their operation will be temporarily affected during construction of the project.
The 36 affected shops are all run by the families and these families will receive compensation at
the displacement price with which they can purchase shops of a similar floor space and structure in
similar locations. The shop owners may choose to purchase shops to continue operation or use the
compensation for other investments.
The two affected shops in Wulong County are operated on rent. The tenants can be resettled in
two ways: in the first place, the demolisher provides the tenants houses that can be rented as
shops including shops of similar location and rent rate and helps them look for and arrange new
production houses. The tenants shall receive a movement allowance at the rate of RMB15/m2. The
owners of both shops shall receive compensation for loss of rent. In the second place, the tenants
shall be compensated for loss of income (including wages) due to discontinuation of operation
during the period of temporary impact and the owners of the two shops shall be paid a
compensation for loss of rent at the rate of RMB20,000 per year, which can be calculated
according to the actual duration of impact.

CHONGOING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK

E.    INCOME REHABILITATION PLAN
The socioeconomic survey shows that, for the affected farmers, the income from land accounts for
13-40% of their total income and the majority of income comes from non-agricultural activities,
accounting for more than 60%. Wages earned by working as migrant laborers in the city constitute
the major source of non-agricultural income, accounting for more than 43% of the total amount. As
the urban environment projects are mostly built on narrow strips of land, most of the farmers will
not have their land completely acquired. The average rate of impact caused by land acquisition is
3% and the highest rate of impact is 32%. Therefore, land acquisition will bring about no major
impact on the income of the affected persons. See Table 7 for detail.

CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Farmers whose land is permanently acquired shall be reasonably compensated at the rate of
RMB21,450-45,000/mu. The affected persons may choose from the following three alternatives for
production resettlement:
1) Reallocation of farmland, by which the farmland is reallocated among the villages and the land
compensation and resettlement subsidy received after reallocation are divided equally among
villagers. Dazu County will adopt the method.
2) Monetary compensation: by which farmers in villages where the per-capita space of farmland
after land acquisition is more than 0.5 mu are resettled by monetary compensation, that is, the
land compensation and resettlement subsidy are paid to the affected persons depending on the
space of land acquisition.
3) Change of status by which farmers in villages where the per-capita space of farmland is less
than 0.5mu are resettled by having their status as agricultural population changed into non-
agricultural population. These people will thus receive a sum of RMB16,000 as land
compensation and resettlement subsidy. After the number of status-changed persons is
decided, the farmland given up by them may be reallocated among villagers remaining in the
village depending on their willingness.
The status-changed farmers affected by land acquisition may be resettled by monetary
compensation, insurance, social security support, etc.
1) Monetary compensation, by which the land compensation and resettlement subsidy are paid to
the status-changed persons to allow them to make a living;
2) Resettlement by basic social endowment insurance, by which those who are above 16 years of
age but have not yet reached the age of retirement specified by the state government may, by
presenting their urban resident register and ID card, apply for the, basic endowment insurance
for urban workers at the local social insurance agency. Those who have secured this type of
insurance and have actually paid the premium for 15 years and longer may receive endowment
insurance money on a monthly basis after they have reached the age of 60 years for men and
55 years for women.
3) Resettlement by social security support, by which those status-changed persons may apply for
the minimum urban resident subsistence-allowance if the average income of them and their
family members living together is lower than the minimum local subsistence level of urban
residents. The level of the allowance is determined according to the cost of clothing, food and
shelter necessary to maintain a decent life for a local urban resident and in consideration of the
cost of water and fuel (coal or gas) and compulsory schooling of their young children. The
standard of urban minimum subsistence allowance in the affected localities are respectively:
RMB185/person/month in Beibei District, RMB145/month in Jiangjin County, Changshou
District, Tongliang County and Bishan County, RMB115/person/month in Wulong County and
RMB130/person/month in Dazu County.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS- 23500321.R4 - AUGUST 2004                     PAGE 12



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
For those farmers losing farmland, the local government will establish a complete labor service
system to provide assistance to them. The relevant labor service agency for the affected people will
be founded one month before land acquisition to help the resettled person get employed through all
possible channels. Such help includes, for example, giving the status-changed persons free access
to the job market, collecting job information from the local sources and providing it to the resettled
persons one month before land acquisition and then publishing such information once a month
afterwards, providing free vocational training to the status-changed persons (Such training is
mainly oriented to the demand of the local job market. For instance, in Dazu County, the training is
oriented to the acquisition of metalworking skills, and in Bishan County, it is oriented to the
acquisition of shoe-making skills, etc.). The labor service agency will also consult the enterprises
being constructed or seeking expansion and provide them with certain preferential incentive
policies (such as being exempted from part of tax if they employ the status-changed persons) in
order to make it easier for these persons to get employed.
F.     REHABILITATION OF VULNERABLE GROUPS
The vulnerable groups refer to those groups of people most easily harmed by these projects as
well as those to whom the environment in which they live makes them unable to adjust themselves
to the changes brought about by the construction of these projects. The vulnerable groups include
mainly impoverished families, families consisting of handicapped persons, families consisting
mainly of women, families consisting of alone-living old people (single and aged more than 65
years and having no legal supporters) and families of ethnic minority people.
The projects will affect 124 persons in 53 families of the vulnerable group including 75 people in 15
impoverished families, 18 people in 18 families having handicapped members, 13 people in 7
families consisting mainly of women, and 18 people in 13 families consisting of old people living
alone, and will affect no families of ethnic minority people.
Except the policies described above, the vulnerable groups shall enjoy the following preferential
policies.
(1) The land compensation and resettlement subsidy may be paid, at their will, to the county public
welfare bureau or county (village) rest house or their children who will take care of them in the rest
of their lives.
(2) Those vulnerable groups affected by house demolition and having difficulty getting adequately
sheltered shall be provided with assistance according to the situation such as by providing cheap-
rent houses, offering vocational training to the laborers in their families and providing them with job
information and guidance to increase their chance of getting employed.
(3) For those vulnerable groups who choose to build their owr houses, the demolisher shall assist
them in building the houses and offer free agricultural technical training to their children and help
them develop agricultural production to increase their income from farming.
(4) Land shall be restored first for those vulnerable groups affected by land occupation.
(5) During construction of the project, prior consideration shall be given to employing the children of
the vulnerable groups to do jobs requiring no special skill.

G.     BUDGET AND IMPLEMENTATION PLAN
The total resettlement budget for constructing the projects is RMB103 million, including RMB38.862
million in making compensation for permanent acquisition of land, accounting for 38%, RMB9.817
million in making compensation for demolishing urban and rural residential houses, accounting for
10%, RMB16.993 million in making compensation for the affected enterprises and institutions,
accounting for 17%, RMB3.512 million in making compensation for the affected shops, accounting
for 3% of the total budget. The total resettlement expense will be included in the cost of the whole
project package. The major source of fund includes the developer own fund and loans of the local
govemments. The budget for each individual project is as shown in Table 8.
The compensation for land acquisition and house demolition is paid to the resettlement agency by
the project owner. The resettlement agency then pays the land compensation and resettlement
subsidy to the affected villages or households. The crop compensation is paid directly to the
affected households. The village leadership divides the land compensation and resettlement
subsidy in different ways. The house compensation is paid to the owner of the house by the
resettlement implementation agency in installments as stipulated in the house demolition and
relocation contract, the compensation for affected enterprises, institutions and shops is paid directly
to their owners, and the compensation for infrastructure, ground attachment and sparse trees
directly to its owner. Those copies of compensation contracts and payment receipts must be kept in
the project owner and county PMOs at the same time. The fund circulation process chart is as
shown in below.

H.        ORGANIZATIONAL ARRANGEMENT
Chongqing Municipal Leading Group for Projects Utilizing World Bank Loans and Chongqing PMO
act as the managing and coordinating agency for land acquisition and house demolition, direct the
county, city and district offices in preparing their respective resettlement action plans according to
the World Bank policies on social security, supervise and monitor the implementation of the
compensation and resettlement plan, and furnish periodic internal monitoring reports on the
implementation of the resettlement plan and submit them to the World Bank.
The district, county and city PMOs are headed by the responsible leaders of the district, county and
city governments and staffed by leaders of the national land and housing administration bureau,
environment protection bureau, water conservation bureau and other agencies. These offices are
mainly responsible for preparing the resettlement action plan of the district, county and city or
entrusting it to a dedicated design institute, coordinate work of the agencies for land acquisition and
resettlement, supervise work on land acquisition and resettlement and furnish periodical internal
monitoring     reports on the      implementation       of the district, city and      county resettlement action          plan
and submit them to Chongqing PMO.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                                                            PAGE 15



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
The owner of each project in the respective districts, cities and counties is the executive agency for
constructing the project and shall, in resettlement activities, designate special-duty personnel to
supervise and manage the process. Its major responsibility includes authorizing the designer to
prepare the resettlement action plan, participating in resettlement surveys, confirming the
resettlement action plan, consigning or organizing resettlement action, supervising and managing
the resettlement implementation, paying money, reporting the progress of resettlement to the
district, city or county PMOs and furnishing internal monitoring reports.
The resettlement-executing agency performs the resettlement work in two ways: firstly, the owner
entrusts the resettlement work to the district, city or county land administration bureau and
demolisher; secondly, the owners carry out the resettlement plan by themselves. Of the eight loan
saving projects, seven's are to be carried out using the first option. The resettlement executing
agency in Dazu County is project owner itself. See Table 9 for detail.
The urban or rural township resettlement work group, village committee and villager group
participate in the project survey and assist in the preparation of the Resettlement Action Plan, take
part in the engineering survey, organize public participation, publicize policies regarding
resettlement, carry out, insect, monitor and record the resettlement activities within the township,
help secure formalities necessary for effecting house demolition and resettlement, participate in
and supervise the acquisition of land, demolition of houses and attached buildings and resettlement
and reconstruction of houses, allocate funds, coordinate and handle contradictions and issues in
the work, organize production, development and other resettlement activities, report the resettled
persons' complaints and suggestions to the superior agency, and provide assistance for the
resettled families in difficulty.

Founded in 1993, Chongqing PMO is highly experienced in managing and implementing WB-
assisted projects. However it is the first time for the WB-assisted project offices of the affected
districts, cities and counties to handle such projects and they lack experience in resettlement
implementation and management. To ensure the smooth implementation of this resettlement action
plan, municipal office will strengthen organizational capability in the following aspects:
1) Staff reinforcement: the organization at each level will be made up of specialized technical
personnel and managerial personnel who must be adequately qualified in technology and
management;

2) Intensified training: since March 2003, experts have been invited several times to train major
staff members of each organization on such subjects as World Bank's operation policy (OP4.12)
regarding involuntary resettlement, laws and regulations on land acquisition and house
demolition, conduction of socioeconomic surveys, and production and livelihood rehabilitation
for resettled persons and further training will be provided for workers involved in the work on
land acquisition and resettlement for constructing the proposed projects, including resettlement
polices, implementation and management of resettlement, resettlement monitoring and
evaluation, etc.;
3) Providing sufficient support in finance and equipment to improve work efficiency;
4) Strengthening the reporting system and intensifying internal supervision and monitoring to
solve any problem found;
5) Establishing an external supervision and evaluation mechanism and an early warning system.
PUBLIC CONSULTATION AND DISCLOSURE
In compliance with the resettlement policies, laws and regulations issued by the central
government, Chongqing municipal government and local governments of districts, cities and
counties involved, in order to protect the legal rights and interests of the resettled persons and
entities, and minimize dissatisfactions and disputes, great importance will be attached to the
participation of the resettled people in the whole process of policy making and plan development
and implementation to widely hear their suggestions and views.
While the settlement plan is being prepared, the plan maker, project owner, each district, city or
county project office, land administration bureau, resettlement office, township government and
village committee has held several discussions with the affected persons before fixing the
compensation rates and resettlement alternatives.
Before the project is executed, the resettlement office will distribute the resettlement booklets
among the affected villages. The affected residents will then obtain the booklets from the
residential committee, village committee, which contains detail on project profile, project impacts,
polices on compensation, project executing institution, channel to lodge complaints and grievances,
etc.
Up to August 2004, the reseKtlement plan reviewed and approved by the World Bank have been
placed in each district, city or county resettlement office and library and public notices issued on
major local newspapers or cable TV so that the affected persons can get a full understanding of the
reseKtlement plan and be aware of their own rights.

CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT

J.     COMPLAINTS AND GRIEVANCES
If the affected person objects the resettlement plan during implementation, he or she may file his or
her complaint orally or in writing to the leaders of the neighborhood committee, township
government and village committee. The latter shall take written record of the complaint and give a
response within one week. If the affected person is unsatisfied with the result, he or she may, upon
receiving the resolution, appeal to the district, and county or city PMOs or Chongqing PMO, which
shall resolve the case within one week. If the affected person is still unsatisfied with the result, he
or she may, upon receiving the resolution, appeal to the district, county or city land administration
agency (monitoring and arbitration agency for land acquisition) or house demolition and
resettlement office for administrative arbitration, which should arbitrate the case within ten days. If
the affected person is still unsatisfied with the result of administrative arbitration, he or she may,
upon receiving the arbitration result, bring a lawsuit to a civil law court in case of objection to any
aspect of the resettlement plan.
K.     MONITORING AND EVALUATING
According to the World Bank's guide for monitoring and evaluating, an internal and external
monitoring mechanism will be established during planning and implementing the proposed
environment projects in Chongqing. Internal monitoring will be carried out by the municipality and
each district, city or county PMOs, while extemal monitoring by an independent supervision and
evaluation agency chosen by competitive.bidding. The supervision and evaluation group shall be
made up of highly experienced resettlement and socioeconomic experts.
The subject for internal monitoring includes mainly: progress of resettlement, compensation for and
rebuilding of resettlement houses, space of land acquisition, compensation for land acquisition,
labor force resettlement, rehabilitation and reconstruction of infrastructure, allocation and use of
resettlement funds, handling of complaints and grievances, staffing of each resettlement agency
and personnel training, working schedule, function performance and efficiency of each resettlement
agency, etc.
The emphasis of external supervision and evaluation is placed on the rehabilitation of production
and living standards of the affected persons, which includes:
1) Monitoring of typical resettled resident households (10%): payment of urban resident
compensation fund, availability of resettlement houses, and income rehabilitation; availability
of house sites for resettlement of rural residents, progress of house construction, payment of
compensation fund, quality of houses constructed, etc.;
2) Monitoring of typical shops (20%): payment of shop compensation fund, availability of
resettlement houses, progress of relocation, rehabilitation of production, and rehabilitation of
employees' income;
3) Monitoring of enterprises and institutions (20%): payment of compensation fund, land
acquisition for new sites, houses construction, progress of relocation, production rehabilitation,
rehabilitation of employees' income.
In addition, it is necessary to monitor resettlement progress, compensation rates and allocation of
fund, capability of executing agencies, depth and effect of public participation by resettled persons,
operation and efficiency of mechanisms handling complaints and grievances, etc.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                     PAGE 18



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGOING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Each district, city or county PMOs will prepare one internal monitoring report every three months
and submit it to Chongqing PMO, which will prepare a year-end summary statement to be
submitted to the World Bank. The independent external monitoring agency will produce one
monitoring report every half a year. The basic survey will be conducted in December 2004 and the
first issue of the monitoring report will be produced in August 2005 and the second issue in
February 2006. Monitoring and assessment reports (Issue 3 to Issue 5) will be submitted from
August 2006 to August 2007.
After the project is completed, post evaluation will be conducted on the basis of monitoring and
evaluation already made and using the relevant theory and method to evaluate the successful
experience and lessons to be learnt in the resettlement of residents, shops, enterprises and
institutions and provide experience usable to later resettlement activities for constructing small city
projects in Chongqing.
L.     REVIEW ON THE IMPLEMENTED RESETTLEMENT OF CUEP
Chongqing Urban Environment Project (CUEP) consists of five components, namely, Chongqing
Urban Waste Water Component, Chongqing Urban Solid Waste Component, Fuling Waste Water
Component, Shizhu Water Supply Component and Wanzhou Water Supply Component. The two
components of Shizhu and Wanzhou did not acquire land and demolish houses and thus no
resettlement involved.
According to the RAP confirmed by WB, totally this project would permanently acquire land of
3550.84mu, demolish house areas of 247184.95M2, affecting 13418 people in 3193 households.
The total budget is RMB762 million. See table 10 for details.

As a joint team, Southwest Transportation University and Chongqing Social Science Institute is
independent monitoring agencies of the project. Up to now, five monitoring reports have been
submitted. These reports revealed that: the project construction has been in smooth progress;
owners and executing agencies of local governments paid compensation in time without delaying,
skimping and embezzling the resettlement fund; the planning, construction, environment of
resettlement sites and house structure are fully consulted with APs, and the income and housing
condition of the APs are a bit better than before; and the resettled are satisfied with the relocation.
At the same time, these reports also put forward that on the resettlement sites of Jiguanshi and
Tangiatuo farming markets were not built up and allocated in time to the APs based on the
resettlement plan. Chongqing municipal government and CPMO have already paid more attention
to the problems, and made a commitment to solve the resettlement problems according to the
action plan agreed by WB,
During the implementation of saving loan project, to draw lessons from the ongoing CUEP is very
necessary. Besides establishing the resettlement external independent monitoring institute, PMOs
should establish resettlement internal monitoring mechanism; reseKtlement implementation
agencies should participate in the RAP preparation, and understand the WB involuntary
resettlement policies. They should implement the resettlement in the light of RAP confirmed by WB,
and periodically submit reseKtlement internal monitoring reports to project owners and PMOs.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                   PAGE 20



CHONGOING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
OBJECTIVE OF THIS RAP AND DEFINITION OF RESETTLEMENT TERMINOLOGY
This Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) is prepared according to the relevant national and local laws
and regulations effective in the People's Republic of China and the clauses in OP4.12: "Involuntary
Resettlement" of World Bank Operation Guidelines. The purpose of preparing the document is "to
provide the affected people with such a resettlement and rehabilitation plan so as to ensure they
benefit from the project and have their living standards improved or at least restored to the pre-
displacement level after the project is completed."
The term "affected people" is defined as follows:
"Affected people" refers to those people whose standard of living is being or will be adversely
affected due to the implementation of the project or affected by the temporary or permanent
acquisition of their ownerships, rights or interests to any houses, lands (including house sites,
farmlands and pastures) or other movables or immovable or the negative effect on their businesses,
takings and jobs or inhabitations and habits.
'Affected people" may either be individuals or legal persons such as enterprises and public
institutions. The definition of "affected people" does not limit the permission of their legal
registration and livelihood or businesses being carried out within the affected area nor limit the
compensation for the damage of their properties and includes the following:
(1) All the people regardless of their legal rights and interests or whether they are present when
their properties are acquired and
(2) People not given permission to reside in a particular area.
Therefore, all these people will be considered and recorded as affected people regardless of their
properties, lands or locations.
If the acquired lands or properties of more than one person or household are to be used or
compensated for, compensation and rehabilitation will be made depending on the damage and
impact received on their rights and living standards. The definition of affected people has a direct
relationship with the adverse impact of the project regardless of their legal rights and interests.
The term "compensation" is defined as follows:
Compensations should be made to all the people affected by the project to improve or at least
restore their living standards and for the damages caused to their properties. The compensation for
damages of properties will be made at the price as if there are bought new and not at a reduced or
discounted price based on depreciation or other reasons. All the affected people should be given
the rights and interests derived from the impacts they receive, and, except for being given the
compensation for the property damage, they should also be subsidized for rehabilitation. Those
who are affected by the project but have no properties, rights and legal permission for residence
and are engaged in businesses, land cultivation or building construction without should be treated
as equal to those who have properties, rights and legal permission for residence and are qualified
to have their livelihood restored and property damages compensated for.
The term "resettlement" is defined as follows:
"Resettlement' refers to the arrangement made for people affected by the project in production or
livelihood activities so that they can benefit from the project. This mainly involves the following:
(1) Movement of shelters;
(2) Seeking reemployment for the affected people;
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS- 23500321 R4 - AUGUST 2004                      PAGE 21



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
(3) Making rehabilitation of (or compensation for) the loss of lands, work places, trees and
infrastructures;
(4) Restituting welfare for those whose living standards (or quality) is adversely affected (such as
harmed by polluting gases) due to land acquisition and resettlement;
(5) Restoring or compensating for the affected private or public enterprises; and
(6) Restoring cultural or public properties adversely affected.
The term "rehabilitation" is defined as follows:
'Rehabilitation" means to bring back the capability of the affected people to continue their
production activities or improve their living standard or at least maintain it at the level before the
project is constructed.
The ultimate purpose of this "Resettlement Action Plan' is to enable those affected by the project to
have their damages compensated so that their living standard is improved or kept at the level
before the project is constructed. To achieve this purpose, the plan outlines rehabilitation measures
so that the affected people can regain their income to enable them to live on. Meanwhile, the
affected business and production resources (including shops and enterprises), public properties,
infrastructures and cultural relics will also be improved or at least restored to the level before the
project is constructed.

1 INTRODUCTION
1.1 BACKGROUND
The Chongqing Urban Environment Project approved by the World Bank in Fiscal Year 2001, has
been designed to address pollution problems in the Municipality by providing a blend of both key
infrastructure investments and institutional reforms. The objective of the Chongqing Urban
Environment Project (CUEP) is to provide a safe environmental setting for the sustainable long-
term economic growth of urban areas in Chongqing Municipality (CM). The project wouid support
the Municipality in implementing the first phase of a long-term urban environmental improvement
program to recover from past environmental degradation, provide an adequate supply of safe water
and maintain water quality at levels that are compatible with the needs of the wider Yangtze River
Basin.

Since approval of the loan ($200 million) it has become apparent that there will be significant
savings from the loan (estimated at approximately $60 to $70 million), which may be re-allocated
for existing and/or new project components. The basis for this estimate is the trend in procurement
activities, namely:
(a) Bid prices of already awarded contracts average between 50 percent and 60 percent of the
estimated prQject costs indicated in the Project Appraisal Document;
(b) Reductions in the scope of works,
(c) Cost reductions arising from refined detailed engineering design, and
(d) Loan savings due to works being completed along with ongoing bund road works, ahead of
schedule using Chongqing's own funds.
1.2 THE CHONGQING URBANISATION & ENVIRONMENT PROJECT (CUEP Il)
As of November 2002, Chongqing Municipality began to enter in a dialogue with the World Bank
concerning a second possible loan to finance both urban and environmental projects in Chongqing.
As initially outlined the project focussed on four broad sectors:
* Infrastructure construction to support the development of business parks;
* Water Supply;
* Bund Roads (including fiood control/protection);
* River Harness (Wastewater and Flood Control/Protection).
A list of the projects initially presented for financing by the World Bank is presented in TABLE 1-1
below.
As the preparation of a number of the below projects was relatively well advanced, it has been
proposed that these projects cowld be possibly financed using the loan savings from the first urban
environment project in Chongqing, the CUEP.

1.3.1 COMPREHENSIVE ENVIRONMENT IMPROVEMENT WORKS OF BACHUAN AND
HUAIYUAN RIVERS IN TONGLIANG COUNTY (REFERRED TO AS THE PROJECT IN
TONGLIANG COUNTY HEREAFTER)
According to the five major strategies (namely west region development strategy, urbanization
strategy, strong industrial county strategy, sustainable development strategy and open-up strategy)
outlined in the 10th five-year plan of Tongliang County, the intensification of the construction of
infrastructures and ecological environment has become an outstandingly important task to perform.
The government of Tongliang County has therefore decided at the right time to appoint Longdu
Water Resources Development Co. Ltd. as the owner of the comprehensive environment
improvement projects of Bachuan and Huaiyuan Rivers, which started the preliminary work on the
project in the spring of 2002. Currently the feasibility study of this project has passed the domestic
appraisal.
The project, after its completion, will improve the production and living environment for the urban
residents and the arrangement of waters, protective embankments, roads and bridges and green
spaces within the 4.8 km2 county seat will be rationalized and complete to exhibit the style of a
modern city. This will further promote the economic development and social progress and quicken
the process of urbanization to achieve the goal of building a well-off society.
1.3.2 COMPREHENSIVE ENVIRONMENT IMPROVEMENT WORKS OF LAIXI RIVER
(LONGSHUI SECTION) IN DAZU COUNTY (REFERRED TO AS THE PROJECT IN DAZU
COUNTY HEREAFTER)
In order to solve the water supply problem facing the people in Dazu and Rongchang Counties,
spur socio-economic development and urban construction, improve the environment along the Laixi
River to promote environmental and ecological protection and lay a foundation for the sustained
development of Dazu County, it is essential to conduct comprehensive improvement of the Laixi
River and so far the feasibility study of the project has been completed and passed the domestic
appraisal.
The purpose of constructing this project is to mitigate the pollution of the water body of the Laixi
River by sewage water from Longshui Township so as to restore the ecological environment of the
river system and improve the condition and quality of living for the people residing alongside the
river.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                     PAGE 30



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
1.3.3 COMPREHENSIVE ENVIRONMENT IMPROVEMENT WORKS OF TAOHUAXI RIVER IN
CHANGSHOU DISTRICT (REFERRED TO AS THE PROJECT IN CHANGSHOU DISTRICT
HEREAFTER)
By 2005, according to the "Urban Master Plan of Changshou District", the priority of work on
environment protection will be given to the prevention and elimination of pollution, protection of the
drinking water resources, deepening the cleaning up and management of industrial wastewater to
achieve the goal of clean production, and curbing pollution by domestic sewage and garbage to put
the ecological environment into a positive cycle. For this reason, the district government of
Changshou has decided at the right time to initiate the comprehensive environment improvement
project of the Taohuaxi River and the feasibility study of the project has now been completed.
The project, once completed, will achieve the goal of comprehensively improving the environment,
effectively solving the problem of water pollution, eliminating the potential threat of floods, and
gradually putting the urban ecological and domestic environment into a positive cycle so as to
promote social progress and economic development, create for the people a favourable
environment in which to work and live, improve the investment atmosphere and realize sustainable
development.
1.3.4 PROJECT IN BISHAN COUNTY (TWO COMPONENTS)
Background information about the urban water supply works in Bishan County seat (referred to as
Project in Bishan County hereafter): The project is intended to improve the water supply capacity in
Bishan County seat and provide a guarantee for constructing the Bisheng-Qinggang-Dingjia
economy corridor by 2010. So far the feasibility study of the project has been completed.
The purpose of the Bishan project is to improve the domestic living quality of the residents in
Bicheng, Puyuan and Shizi Townships of Bishan County and heighten the general level of
urbanization in these townships to support their sustainable development.
Background information about the comprehensive environment improvement project of Binan River
in Bishan County (referred to as Binan River project hereafter): According to the "10th five-year
plan for national and social development of Bishan County" passed at the 4th session of the 13th
people's congress of Bishan County on February 20, 2002, the Binan River Project in Bishan
County was officially included in the schedule of work to be performed in the near future. Now the
project has been registered and approved and feasibility study of the project is under way.
The project serves the purpose of effectively improving the flood resisting capability of the
riverbanks to protect people living along either side of the river against flood damages and
meanwhile, by improving the riverbanks, bettering the road transportation condition and urban and
domestic living environment and perfecting the overall function of the city.

CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
1.3.5 COMPREHENSIVE ENVIRONMENT IMPROVEMENT PROJECT ALONG RIVERSIDES IN
WULONG COUNTY (REFERRED TO AS THE PROJECT IN WULONG COUNTY
HEREAFTER)
According to the development strategy of "being based in the Three Gorges Area, getting support
from Chongqing, developing tourism as the pioneering industry, rationalizing the arrangement of
urban area along both rivers and achieving economic takeoff from both flanks" and to achieve the
goal of building Wulong County into an ecologically and economically strong county where the local
economy, population and environment find harmonious development, the CPC committee and
govemment of Wulong County had decided at the right time to construct the "project of riverbank
roads construction and comprehensive improvement works for flood prevention in Wulong County".
Currently the feasibility study of the project has been completed.
T he purpose of this project is to improve the flood resistance of both banks of the Wujiang River
from occurring once every two years to once every 20 years so as to ensure normal life of
residents and economic construction in the countryseat, improve the water and land transport
condition, enable the riverbank road to function as the main road, complete the wharf facilities,
beautify the city, improve the sightseeing and investment atmosphere, spur economic construction
and quicken the urbanization process.
1.3.6 WATER SUPPLY WORKS IN SHUANGFU TOWNSHIP, JIANGJIN. CITY (REFERRED TO
AS THE PROJECT IN JIANGJIN CITY HEREAFTER)
The fact that there is no sufficient source of raw water nearby in Shuangfu Township and the
volume and sanitation level of the present water source cannot meet the demand of people for
domestic life and economic development, the serious shortage of water and absence of drinking
water source meeting the national standard have combined to constitute a grave hindrance to the
local socio-economic development. Therefore, there is an urgent need for constructing this project.
Currently the feasibility study of the project has been completed.
The project is mainly meant to provide water supply for production in the industrial park area of
Shuangfu Township, improve the condition of water supply for domestic use for residents in
Shuangxi, Jinfu, Xiangtang and Shengquan villages of Shuangfu Township, bring up the level of
urbanization of the area and promote the industrial production and socio-economic development of
the region.
1.3.7 WATER SUPPLY WORKS IN DONGYANG, BEIBEI DISTRICT (REFERRED TO AS THE
PROJECT IN BEIBEI DISTRICT HEREAFTER)
The existing water supply facilities are far from being able to meet the increasing demand for local
economic development and domestic life of the local people, and the backward situation
constitutes a major factor hindering local socio-economic development and improvement of living
standard of the local people. Therefore there is an urgent call for the construction of water supply
system in Dongyang, Beibei District and the feasibility study of the projects have now been
completed.
The project, after completion, is able to ensure water supply for production and domestic life in the
planned area of Dongyang, the seat of Beibei District.

1.5 AREAS BENEFITING FROM AND AFFECTED BY THE PROJECT
An area totalling 1,329 km2 will be involved for constructing this project, which will bring about a
direct benefit to as many as 1,500,000 people. The project, if successfully constructed, will no
doubt spur the sustainable development of local society and economy in the project area.
By land acquisition (or occupation) and house demolition, this project will affect 46 villages in 8
rural townships of 7 counties (cities or districts) totaling 4,525 people in 1,146 households, of which
420 people in 122 households will be affected both by land acquisition and house demolition.
1.6 SOCIOECONOMIC BACKGROUND OF THE AFFECTED AREAS
The "2003 Chongqing WB loan saving projects" (or, in full, Loan Saving Projects under Chongqing
Urban Environment Project in 2003) is a project group consisting of 8 components, namely, 5
environment improvement projects and 3 water supply projects. These projects are located in the
metropolitan area and its western and northeastern suburbs. The fundamental socio-economic
data of the 7 districts (or cities) involved are as listed in below:

Tongliang County is located in the west of Chongqing with a total area of 1,;343 km2. It belongs to
the wet subtropical seasonal-wind prevailing climatic zone with a mild climate and rich in rainfall
and resources.
Dazu County is located in the southeastern part of the Sichuan Basin and the west of Chongqing. It
borders Tongliang County in the east, Yongchuan City and Rongchang                 County in the south,
Sichuan Province's Anyue County in the west and Tongnan County in the north with a total area of
1,399.34 km2.

Changshou District is located in the northeastern suburbs of the metropolitan area of Chongqing
and 76km away from the downtown area. It has a territory of 1,415.49km2 and consists of 633
villages and neighbourhoods in 36 rural and urban townships. The total population of the district
was 877,600 by the end of 2001.
Bishan County is located in the west of Chongqing and is known as the traffic gate in the western
part of Chongqing as it is located at the junction point of the G319 national highway route with the
provincial highway route and is only 44km away from the downtown area.
Wulong County is located on the southeastern rim of Chongqing in fold jointly formed by the
Daloushan and Wuling mountain ranges of the Yunnan-Guizhou plateau. The territory lies between
107013'-108056'E and 29002'-29040'N and measures 82.7km long from east to west and 75 km
wide from north to south. It borders Pengshui in the east, Guizhou Province's Daozhen County in
the south, Nanchuan County and Fuling District in the west and Fengdu County in the north.
Jiangjin City's Shuangfu Township is located by the side of the Jin-Ma highway route and 3km
away from the Zouma exit of the Chongqing-Chengdu expressway. Shuangfu township consists of
Shuangxi, Jinfu, Xiangtang and other neighbourhoods, or which Shuangxi and Jinfu is within the
boundary of the planned Shuangfu Township industrial park area.
Beibei District is located to the northwest of Chongqing and is 45km away from the metropolitan
area of Chongqing. The district covers a total area of 755km2 and Dongyang Township is located
in the north by the northern side of the Jialing River.
1.7 MEASURES TO MINIMIZE IMPACT CAUSED BY THE PROJECT
During the periods of planning, designing, construction and resident resettlement, the designer and
project owner have acquired some effective measures to minimize the impact of the project on the
local society and economy of the project area.
1.7.1 PROJECT PLANNING AND DESIGNING PERIOD
Optimise the design to avoid as much as possible densely populated areas or multi-story or high
buildings as an effort to minimize the area of land acquisition and house demolition and
resettlement and the number of non-voluntary resettlement of residents.
When designing the sewage treatment plants and water supply plants, a number of site alternatives
are provided to find out the one involving the least demolition and resettlement of houses.
When planning green belts and pedestrian passageways, their widths have been determined
section by section according to the actual situation to avoid as much as possible demolishing and
relocating permanent buildings within the project area.
When planning the pressurizing pump stations, due considerations have been given to the
technical requirement for water supply pipeline route and the actual topographical conditions along
the route and the sites chosen are far from the residential area. This not only makes it easier to lay
out the pipeline but also minimizes the impact of the project on the domestic life and production
activities of the local residents.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                  PAGE 36



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
The water delivery and distribution pipelines will be laid along the highway route or follow the
existing pipeline route to minimize land acquisition and house demolition and avoid affecting the
local residents' domestic life and production. In addition, under the condition of ensuring safe
supply of water, single pipeline will be adopted to minimize the space needed for construction and
transportation. In places along the highway route where there are residential houses and it is
impossible to lay pipes, a bypass route will be followed to void resettlement of residents.
1.7.2 CONSTRUCTION PERIOD
At the construction period, special efforts such as improving the construction techniques,
strengthening the management and separate operation and separate rehabilitation will be made to
minimize the impact on the local people caused by land acquisition and construction operations
and at the same time make it convenient for the affected people to proceed with their work and
daily lives.
Temporary occupation of land will be minimized or avoided and exploitation of local materials for
construction will be avoided. Materials will be purchased from the market. All the temporary
buildings for construction will be arranged in the range of acquired land to avoid additional
occupation of land. Though temporary excavation and occupation are unavoidable in pipeline
construction, positive measures will be taken to minimize the impact.
The construction period and the time of land occupation will be shortened as much as possible to
minimize the impact on the shop business of the affected farmers.
Rehabilitation of demolished facilities will be planned and arranged in advance. In actual practice,
the local conditions will be made the best use of to ensure safety, effectiveness, promptness and
accuracy and minimize the adverse effect on the people living nearby.
If technically feasible, priority will be given to using local transport facilities and labour services so
that the affected local people can benefit from the project.
1.7.3 LAND ACQUISITION AND RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN AND ITS
IMPLEMENTATION PERIOD
When land acquisition and resettlement of people are inevitable, the following measures will be
acquired to minimize the impact on the local people.
Ensure that every affected group of people get the compensation for all their damages at a price as
if the property were purchased new and that they are properly resettled and restored to share the
benefit brought about by the project.
On the basis of the socio-economic survey and further analysis of the local situation, a reasonable
and practicable resettlement plan should be prepared to minimise the projects impacts of house
demolition and land acquisition and ensure resettled persons' income rehabilitation.
Make detailed plans to safeguard the interests of the resettled persons, announce the policies and
practices about compensation in time, accept openly the claims of the resettled persons and the
resettlement office will solve any problem occurring through consultation with the resettled local
people to ensure they receive no or the least impact on their domestic lives.
Encourage public participation and accept the monitoring of the masses
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS- 23500321.R4 - AUGUST 2004                      PAGE 37



CHONGOING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGOING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Strengthen internal and external monitoring and monitoring, establish an efficient and free
feedback mechanism and channel. The actual situation of the work on resettlement will be
supervised and evaluated by an independent supervising agency. The time for handling feedbacks
will be shortened as much as possible to ensure that all the problems occurring during the project
executing process receive timely solutions.

2 IMPACTS OF THE PROJECT
To understand the impact of the project, the project office, in compliance with the requirement of
the World Bank, formed a special survey team to conduct detailed investigations into the families of
the affected people, enterprises, institutions and shops from June 2003 to March 2004. The survey
work was done in a combination of door-to-door visits and face-to-face interviews and the content
of survey included such details as the area and type of acquired land, affected people, and number
of households, number of family members, area of houses to be resettled and number of workers
in enterprises, institutions and shops. During the survey into the tangible impact of demolition and
resettlement involved in executing the project, the affected people participated in the work. The
survey team listened to the comments of the residents and owners of enterprises, institutions and
shops on land acquisition, house demolition and resident resettlement and extensive discussions
were held.
By land acquisition (or occupation) and house demolition, this project will affect 46 villages in 8
rural townships of 7 counties (cities or districts) totaling 4,525 people in 1,146 households, of which
420 people in 122 households will be affected both by land acquisition and house demolition.
In the 46 villages of 8 rural townships of 7 counties (cities or districts) to be affected by the project,
altogether 1,962.5 mu of land will be acquired and occupied and 1,595.8 mu of land permanently
acquired, of which 1,149.3 mu is collective-owned land (including 1048.5 mu of farmland), 391.5
mu is state-owned land and 55 mu of land to be used by enterprises for construction, and a total of
366.8 mu of land will be temporarily occupied, including 189.4 mu of farmland. The land acquisition
(or occupation) will affect a total of 3,807 people in 1,080 households, of which 3,142 people in 890
households will be permanently affected.
By house demolition and resettlement, the project will affect 188 urban and rural families, 18
enterprises and institutions, and 38 shops. Houses totalling 42,514.2m2 in floor space will be
demolished and 1,138 people will be affected.
Rural houses holding 420 people in 122 families will be demolished and resettled with a total area
of 16,283.1m2, including 8,684.4m2 of brick+concrete structure houses, 4,839.2m2 of brick+wood
structure houses, 821.2m2 of earth+wood structure houses and 1,938.3m2 of simple -structure
houses. Altogether 330 urban residents in 66 households will be affected with houses to be
demolished and resettled totalling an area of 11,288.9m2, including 4,084.4m2 of brick+concrete
structure houses, 5,710.9m2 of brick+wood structure houses and 1,494.6m2 of simple structure
houses.
The project will affect 138 people in 15 enterprises. The houses of enterprises to be demolished
and resettled total a floor space of 8,162m2 including 3,391m2 brick+concrete structure .houses,
2,239.2m2 of brick+wood structure houses, 811.54m2 of earth+wood structure houses and
1,720m2 of simple structure houses. The project will affect 70 people in 3 institutions and houses to
be demolished and resettled total a floor space of 4,638m2 including 4,590m2. brick+concrete
structure houses and 48m2 of brick+wood structure houses. A total of 180 people in 38 commercial
shops will be affected by the project and 2,142m2 of shops to be demolished and resettled,
including 975m2 brick+concrete structure houses, 608m2 of brick+wood structure houses and
559m2 of simple structure houses.
The project will affect 124 people in 53 households of the vulnerable group, including 36
households in rural areas and 17 in urban areas.
In addition, the project will affect 33 varieties of ground attachments and public facilities.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 R4 - AUGUST 2004                     PAGE 39

2.1 PERMANENT LAND ACQUISITION AND TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
In the 46 villages of 8 rural townships of 7 counties (cities or districts) to be affected by the project,
altogether 1,962.5 mu of land will be acquired and occupied affecting 3,807 people in 1,080
households.
Of the 1,595.8 mu of land permanently acquired, 1,149.3 mu is collective-owned land (including
1048.5 mu of farmland), 391.5 mu is state-owned land and 55 mu of land to be used by enterprises
for construction, affecting 3,142 people in 890 households. See TABLE 2-1 for detail.
Of the 366.8 mu of temporarily occupied land, 189.4 mu are farmland, affecting 665 people in 190
households. See TABLE 2-2 for detail.
2.2 RESIDENTIAL HOUSES OF AFFECTED PEOPLE
2.2.1 HOUSES OF AFFECTED RURAL RESIDENTS
This project will affect 420 rural residents in 122 households and the total area of rural houses to
be demolished and resettled is 16,283.1m2, including 8,684.4m2 of brick+concrete structure
houses, 4,839.2m2 of brick+wood structure houses, 821.2m2 of earth+wood structure houses and
1,938.3m2 of simple structure houses. In addition, attachments to some of the houses will also be
affected. See
TABLE 2-3 for detail.
2.2.2 HOUSES OF AFFECTED URBAN RESIDENTS
This project will affect 330 urban residents in 66 households and the total area of rural houses to
be demolished and resettled is 11,288.9m2, including 4084.4m2 of brick+concrete structure
houses, 5,709.9m2 of brick+wood structure houses and 1,494.6m2 of simple structure houses. In
addition, attachments to some of the houses will also be affected. See TABLE 2-4 for detail.
2.3 AFFECTED ENTERPRISES
This project will affect 15 enterprises. It is found in the survey that of these affected enterprises,
only six need to be resettled, three ones are only affected by land acquisition, some of them have
been shut down or moved to elsewhere for years except a few still in operation. In their places
remain only the empty workshops to be demolished. Altogether 8,162m2 of enterprise houses need
to be demolished and resettled, including 3,391m2 of brick+concrete structure houses, 2,239m2 of
brick+wood structure houses, 812m2 of earth+wood structure houses and 1,720m2 of simple
structure houses. In addition, attachments to some of the houses will also be affected. See TABLE
2-5 for detail.

2.4 AFFECTED INSTITUTIONS
This project will affect three institutions and altogether 4,638m2 of their houses need to be
demolished and resettled, including 4,590m2 of brick+concrete structure houses and 48m2 of
brick+wood structures houses. See TABLE 2-6 for detail.
2.5 AFFECTED SHOPS
This project will affect 38 shops with altogether 2,142m2 of shop houses to be demolished and
resettled, including 975m2 of brick+concrete structure houses, 608m2 of brick+wood structures
houses and 559m2 of simple structures houses. See TABLE 2-7 for detail.
2.6 AFFECTED POPULATION
The permanent acquisition of rural public land for this project will involve 36 villages in 8 townships,
affecting 3,142 people in 890 households including 1,963 people to be resettled by means of
production. The temporary occupation of land will involve 42 villages in 8 townships and last for a
period of 3-12 months, which will temporarily affect 665 people in 190 households. The demolition
of urban residential houses will affect 330 people in 66 households and the demolition of rural
residential houses will affect 420 people in 122 households. Altogether 15 enterprises are affected,
affecting 138 people and 3 institutions affected, affecting 70 people. Altogether 38 shops are
affected, affecting 180 people. During the process, 420 people in 112 households will be affected
both by land acquisition and house demolition. The actual number of affected population is 4,525
people in 1,146 households. See TABLE 2-8 for detail.
2.7 VULNERABLE GROUPS AFFECTED
The vulnerable groups are the most easily harmed groups of the persons affected by the project.
The environment in which they live makes them unable to adjust themselves to the changes
brought about by the construction of the project. The vulnerable groups mainly include
impoverished families, families consisting handicapped persons, families consisting mainly of
women, families consisting of alone-living old people (single and aged more than 65 years and
having no legal supporters) and families of ethnic minority people.
The socio-economic survey shows that of the 124 people in 53 households of the vulnerable
groups affected, there are 75 people in 15 impoverished families, 18 people in 18 families having
handicapped members, 13 people in 7 families consisting mainly of women, and 18 people in 13
families consisting of old people living alone, and no families of ethnic minority people. See
TABLE 2-9 for detail.
2.8 AFFECTED INFRASTRUCTURE AND GROUND ATTACHMENTS
The project will affect 33 varieties of ground attachments and public facilities. See TABLE 2-10 for
detail.

3 SOCIO-ECONOMIC SURVEY OF PEOPLE AND UNITS AFFECTED
To further understand the socio-economic situation of the affected area and obtain
fundamental facts about the affected people, the project office in compliance with the
requirement of the World Bank carried out a preliminary survey of the socio-
economic situation of the affected area in April 2003 to provide data for analysis. In
September 2003, the project office, while continuing investigations into the quantity
of tangible work, conducted a sample survey of the socio-economic situations of the
affected families, enterprises, institutions and shops. The survey took the form of
questionnaires and interviews and involved 1,848 rural residents (accounting for
40% of the total affected population), 270 urban residents (accounting for 38% of the
affected population), 18 enterprises and institutions (accounting for 100% of the total
number) and 38 shops (accounting for 100% of the total number).
3.1 FUNDAMENTAL FACTS ABOUT THE AFFECTED NATURAL VILLAGES
The permanent land acquisition for the project will affect 36 villages in 8 townships of
Chongqing. The socio-economic situations of these villages are listed in below
TABLE 3-1.
