From TABLE 6-7, it can be seen that Mingugang Village has the largest space of acquired land,
which is 56.76 mu, affecting 118 people and 82 people need to be resettled by production, and that

and 7 people need to be resettled by production. Mingguang Village has 1 group, where has 2867
people and 2208mu farmland. The project will acquire 56.76 mu of farmland, accounting for 2.6%
of the total farmland, which affects 118 people, and 82 need to be resettlement by production. The
per-capita annual income of Mingguang Village is RMB3250, including industrial income RMB2275,
agricultural income RMB975 that accounts for 30% of the total income. If the average annual
turnover of one mu of farmland is RMB500, the per-capita annual income will reduce by RMB132,
less than 1%.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                    PAGE 1 1 1



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
From the above analysis, it can be seen that the impact of land acquisition on the farmers' total
income will be limited. The survey reveals that the farmers in these villages rely very little on the
farmland, which seems to have lost its appeal to them. At present, more than 90% of the villagers
are engaged in the metal ware industry and about 50% of them run small metal ware plants in their
houses. Those who do not run metal ware workshops in their houses normally have their family
members working in the metal ware enterprises in the urban area nearby. The income from running
their own businesses and working in the enterprises account for 81% of the villagers' non-
agriculture income and their income from farming constitutes a fairly small part. Moreover, most of
them now do not work in the field themselves but instead hire other people to do it from them. It
can be said definitely that the livelihood of farmers. living in the project area will not change
significantly due to land acquisition.
6.3.1.2   REHABILITATION OF INCOME
By extensive discussions with the villagers, it is decided that they will be resettled by reallocation of
farmland and the land compensation and resettlement subsidy will be paid equally to each
household.
The affected villages can get a total amount of RMB3.19 million as compensation for land
acquisition and subsidy for resettlement, of which Mingguang Village gets RMB1.218 million,
Xingguang Village RMB0.423 million, Yujian Village RMBO.066 million, Longdong Village
RMB0.751 million and Yongyi Village 0.734 million. The land compensation and resettlement
subsidy for each mu is RMB21, 450-40,800. Based on the current deposit interest rate 2.79%
above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%, the real deposit rate is 2.232%. If the affected
deposit the compensation RMB21,450-40,800 in the bank for 50 years, they will get about
RMB713-1458 each year, which is more than their current yearly net income RMB600(RMB220)
from dry land(paddy field).
After receiving the compensation, the villagers may continue to invest in small metal ware
workshops. This will help them make their current income level of RMB600-700 per month even
higher. Those villagers (accounting for about 10% of the total population) who live on farming can
expect to get a high income from agriculture by renting the farmland of other villagers.
Longshui Township has a long history in making metal ware products the business is fairly large in
scale with a complete sales network in operation. Currently some 50,000 people are engaged in
this industry, which turns out products of 20,000 sizes in 200 varieties and 12 categories.
Advanced technologies are widely employed in the hardening centre, surface-treating centre and
grinding centre. Some famous brands like Jinzhong, Yonghong and Wangsheng are selling well on
both the domestic and overseas markets. The metal transaction market, metal ware market and
metal ware tourist centre have now been constructed and put into operation. With an annual sales
volume of RMB1, 800 million, Longshui Township has become the largest production. and
distribution centre for small metal ware in Southwest China.
There are a number of enterprises around the affected villages, which are doing quite well. The
owners of these enterprises have promised that they will provide some jobs for the labourers in the
affected villages. See TABLE 6-8 for statistics of these enterprises.

6.3.2 REHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
Temporary occupation of land for constructing the project will affect five villages. Altogether 27.6
mu of land will be temporarily occupied; the compensation for temporary land occupation will be
made according to the annual yield of these dry fields. Half a year of occupation will be
compensated for as one whole year with the per-mu 'compensation being RMB1, 800. Since the
project will temporarily occupy the land will last for 6 months, the loss of yield is then RMB1,
000-1200/mu as the period is regarded as one year. Therefore, the compensation received is more
than the actual loss caused and the farmer' livelihood will not be affected by the temporary
occupation of land.
As for the rehabilitation of land temporarily occupied, a preliminary agreement has been reached
between the affected villages and the project executor, which stipulates that the constructor shall
smooth the land, loosen the ground compacted by engineering machinery and improve the quality
of soil and the land-administration agency will conduct acceptance of the restored land.

affecting 298 people, with a total floor space of 10,345.09 m2.
All the houses of these urban residents affected by the project are above 45m2 in space. See
TABLE 6-9 for statistics of the space distribution of the houses.

6.3.5 RESETTLEMENT OF AFFECTED ENTERPRISES
The project will cause two enterprises to be resettled, affecting 38 people, and 1,993.71 m2 of
houses will have to be demolished.
The two affected enterprises are Grease Refinery and Post And Communication Equipment Plant,
which houses will be completely demolished. According to the compensation rates, the enterprises
will get compensation at the rate of RMB226/m2 for their brick+concrete structure houses and
RMB205/m2 for brick+wood structure houses, and be paid compensation at the rate of RMB1 15/M2
for house lands, and be paid for the damage of facilities and financial subsidies for resettlement
and reconstruction. According to the general plan of Longshui Township authorities, the affected
enterprises will be resettled by monetary compensation in the industrial park area of the township.
The affected enterprises can buy the land of the industry park at preferential prices (RMB8O, 000-
120,000/mu). The compensation enables them to rebuild new factories in the industry park. The
resettled enterprises may then make preparations for reconstruction in advance so that
reconstruction takes place before demolition to minimize impact on the enterprise and employee.
Longshui industrial park was approved in 2003 by Chongqing municipal government as one of
Chongqing's 30 feature industrial parks. The park covers a planned area of 6 square kilometres. At
present, construction of the first 1.55 km2 of the park has been initiated, of which 0.78 km2 has
been completed. Currently 93 enterprises have moved into the area, generating an annual
industrial output value of RMB520 million, sales income of RMB478 million and profit of RMB118
million.
See Table 6.11 for the resettlement of affected enterprises.

6.3.6 RESETTLEMENT OF AFFECTED SHOPS
The project will cause 34 shops to be demolished and resettled, affecting 164 people, with a total
space of 1,746.68 m2. These shops have the following features: (1) made from residential houses
along the road or riverside, (2) run by the owners themselves and helped basically by the their
family members, and (3) engaged in metal ware products.
The socio-economic survey involved inquiries into the preferences of the shop owners concerning
resettlement. Through discussions between the demolisher and shop owners in consideration of
the actual condition of the places where the shops are located, it is decided that the resettlement
will take the form of monetary compensation.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                      PAGE 115

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
After demolition and resettlement, the shop owners will receive house compensation (at the rate of
RMB1,980/m2 for brick+concrete structure houses, RMB1,780/m2 for brick+wood structure houses
and RMB1,280/M2 for simple structure houses, all including land price). The financial subsidy for
movement of facilities and compensation for damages caused by closure of business will be
amount to a total amount of RMB3.2569 million and this means that each shop can get RMB63,
000 on the average. The shop owners may use this compensation money to purchase business
houses of better location and space (Longshui Teacher's st., business side walk st.) in Longshui
Township. See TABLE 6-12 for information about the shop market in Longshui Township.
The shops affected by the project will be resettled in Nanyuan residential area, which was
developed by Dazu Nanyuan Real Estate Co. and has a total floor space of 12,00Om2. The average
selling price of the houses is RMB36G/m2. The houses have been designed into different layouts
with sizes ranging from tens of square meters to more than one hundred square meters to suit the
requirements of the resettled families. The residential area is complete with water, power and gas
supplies, transport facilities and communication and cable TV systems. Schools, post offices,
banks, grocery market, bus stops, hospitals and other infrastructures have been built around the
area to convenience the residents.
The employees of the demolished shops are mostly family members of the owner except for a very
few migrant workers. The project executing agent will inform these migrant workers 2 months
before land acquisition takes place to allow enough time for them to get reemployed. Rescannable
compensation will be made for losses caused during movement and closure of business at the rate
of RMB120/M2 depending on the operation of these shops. As the shops in Longshui Township are
engaged mostly in metal ware industry and the places to which the shops are moved are all busy
areas of the township, these affected shop owners can perfectly expect an income level not lower
than before as long as they properly manage their business in their new houses.
See TABLE 6-12 for the resettlement of affected shops.

labourers, 5 families with handicapped members, 3 families consisting mainly of women and 2
families consisting of old people living alone. The impoverished families are those who have laid-

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Of the affected vulnerable group's families, four are rural families with three (affected by land
acquisition) in Mingguang Village and one (affected by both land acquisition and house demolition)
in Xingguang, including 3 handicapped persons and I impoverished person. The source of their
family income is chiefly farming. If the village authorities launch the collective land development
plan such as growing vegetables on a large scale, they will give priority to hiring them or renting the
land of the vulnerable group' families, and priority will be given to training the labourers of the three
families in skills and then arranging them to work in the enterprises. As for the impoverished family
in Xingguang Village, the village leadership will help them build their own house.
The other vulnerable group's families are all urban families affected by house demolition. As their
houses are mostly larger than 80m2 in floor space, according to the compensation rates, the money
they receive will be enough to enable them to purchase new or second-hand houses. For those
whose houses area is below 50m2, if troubled by sheer poverty and unable to afford to buy houses,
the government will provide them with cheap rental houses, which are chiefly located on Longgu
Road and Gunang Street. These houses are within 80-90 m2 in floor space and monthly cost
M22
RMB1.2/m for brick+concrete structure and RMBO.6/m2 for brick+wood structure. Though cheap
in rent, these houses are located in places with convenient transport systems and complete
supplementary facilities such as shopping centres, hospitals and schools to ensure the quality of
the vulnerable group's livelihood. In comparison with their former houses demolished, these
houses are superior in all aspects.
On the other hand, for the surplus labourers in the vulnerable group's families, the government will
give priority to arranging them to work in the local enterprises. As Longshui Township has metal
ware product as its major industry and boasts the iargest metal ware market in China, it poses no
problem to arrange a few labourers from the vulnerable group's families.
Following the custom of respecting and caring about the old in Longshui Township, the government
will pay visit to the affected people's homes in all major traditional holidays. Through such visits,
the government is able to know how this vulnerable group are living and find out the problems they
have in daily life and feed back the information to the project owner and independent supervisor.
6.3.8 REHABILITATION OF AFFECTED INFRASTRUCTURES AND GROUND ATTACHMENTS
(1) The affected power poles in Mingguang Village are used to supply power to the farmers'
homes nearby and pumps for irrigation and will lose their function with the land being occupied.
The loss incurred will be compensated for by monetary means.
(2) The toilet is used by the residents living nearby and will lose its function with the land being
acquired. The project owner will compensate its owner for the loss.
(3) The stone. pavement demolished will be replaced by new embankment.
(4) The wharf is a simple passenger wharf and will be rebuilt when constructing the embankment.
(5) The fruit trees and bamboos will be compensated for by monetary means during land
clearance.
(6) The natural gas pipeline and power line will not be demolished until they are constructed in
other suitable locations so as to minimize impact on the residents around the construction area.

6.4 PROJECT IN CHANGSHOU DISTRICT
The project will acquire 243.74 mu of land including 14.5 mu of enterprise land for permanent use
and 94.82 mu of land for temporary use, affecting 189 people in 56 households, and cause
7,941.9m2 of houses to be demolished, affecting 459 people in 123 households, and 194 people
need to be resettled by production.
6.4.1 REHABILITATION OF PERMANENT LAND ACQUISITION

The project will acquire 243.74 mu of land for permanent use including 186.78 mu of farmland and
0.8 mu of fishpond, affecting 277 people in two villages in Duzhou Township and three villages in
Fenghuang Township and 194 people need to be resettled by production.

From TABLE 6-14, it can be seen that the percentage of per-capita space of farmland to be
affected is 5%-9% and Madao Village will receive the heaviest impact of land acquisition. The
village will have 18 mu of farmland to be acquired, accounting for 14.6% of the total space of
farmland and 23 people will be affected and 16 labourers need to be resettled by production. After
acquisition, the per-capita space of farmland will become 0.89mu, down by 9%. If the average
annual per-mu yield of the farmland is RMB500, land acquisition will cause the yield to drop by
RMB45. As the net per-capita income of this village was RMB2, 487 in 2003, land acquisition will
bring it down by 2%.
The above analysis shows reveals the fact that land acquisition has no major impact on the per-
capita income of all the affected villages. Moreover, about 20% of the labourers in each of the five
villages no longer rely on their land for making a living. The income they get by working as migrant
workers accounts for 50% of their total income. Therefore, land acquisition does not constitute a
major impact on the villagers.

CHONGOING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
6.4.1.2   REHABILITATION OF INCOME
(1) Resettlement plan
Through extensive consultations with the affected villagers, resettlement will be arranged in the
following ways:
6 Changing status
As all the five affected villages are located in the planned area for construction of the county seat,
the land will be acquired gradually in the coming years in the ongoing urbanization process.
Therefore, resettlement of the affected villagers may take the form of changing status depending
on the actual condition and villagers' willingness. For those who can have their status changed but
are unwilling to do so, the village committee will reallocate land among the villagers, that is, to
allocate farmland give up by villagers not affected by land acquisition but are willing to have their
status changed to the former and the latter will have their status changed and receive the land
compensation and resettlement subsidy. The status-changed persons will receive a total amount of
RMB16,000 as land compensation and resettlement subsidy.
Q Monetary compensation
The project-executing agency will pay compensation to farmers who choose to stay in the rural
area for farming rather than having their status changed according to the space of land taken from
them. The five affected villages may receive a total amount of RMB5.2634 million as land
compensation and resettlement subsidy, including RMB3.175 million for Yanqiao Villager,
RmB0.963 million for Xinghua Village, RMBO.395 million for Huohua Village, RMBO.227 million for
Kejiaping Village and RMB0.504 million for Maodao.
Each mu of land taken can be compensated for RMB 28,000. Based on the current deposit interest
rate 2.79% above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%, the real deposit rate is 2.232%. If the
affected deposit the compensation RMB28, 000 in the bank for 50 years, they will get about
RMB930 each year, which is more than their current yearly net income RMB650 from cultivated
land.
(Livelihood support
The status-changed persons may enjoy the basic endowment insurance and minimum subsistence
allowance for urban residents. Those who have secured basic endowment insurance and have
actually paid the premium for 15 years and longer may receive endowment insurance money on a
monthly basis after they have reached the age of 60 years (for men) and 55 years (for women). In
Changshou District, the minimum subsistence allowance is paid RMB145/month, which is more
than their average annual income of RMB1,000 from farming.
For those villagers who have chosen to get resettled by receiving monetary compensation and
whose families include surplus labourers, the village committee will provide them with training on
agricultural production technology and help them restructure their farming business to improve
income, such as developing greenhouse vegetable planting using the advantage of being close to
the urban area.
The local government will establish a complete labour service system to provide assistance to the
affected villagers such as providing them with information on employment, vocational training,
consultation with the local enterprises, etc. to pave the way for them to get employed.
The five affected villages are close to the cities and most of them are located within the planned
area for construction of the new city. The construction of the new city and the new founded
enterprises and those seeking expansion in the development zones provide a lot of job
opportunities for the rural labour force (See TABLE 6-15). The local government will help the
affected labourers to get employment through training, providing employment information and
discussions with the enterprises. In this way, they can get a monthly wage of RMB400-800.

6.4.2 REHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
This project will occupy 94.82 mu of land for temporary use including 84.5 mu of collective-owned
land and 10.32 mu of state-owned land Crop compensation for the land temporarily occupied will
be paid in such as manner that the loss in one year of occupation will be compensated for as 2.5
quarters, which means a total sum of RMB25 million in compensation. Constructing the project will
occupy the land for about o'ne year and the compensation obtained is much higher than the actual
loss as the average annual output value of the farmland is only RMB1, 600 per mu. Therefore, the
farmers' livelihood will not be affected.
After the project is completed, the constructor will re-cultivate the farmland occupied and return it to
the village and group, and the village and group organize to check and accept.
6.4.3 RESETTLEMENT OF RURAL RESIDENTS
The resettlement of rural residents' houses for constructing this project in will involve 189 people in
56 households of 7 villages in Duzhou and Fengcheng Townships. Altogether 7,941.9 m2 of houses
will be demolished. Residents whose houses have been demolished will be resettled by monetary
compensation (the standard being RMB215 per m2 for brick+concrete structure houses, RMB190
per m2 for brick+wood structure houses and RMB50 per m2 for simple structure houses). The
affected people receiving the compensation money have three alternatives to make, namely, to
construct their own houses on sites provided free by the demolish, purchase resettlement houses
at a preferential price and purchase commercial houses. In the former case, the resettlement
agency shall pay compensation to the owner of the house demolished and at the same time
provide him free of charge with a house site. In the latter two cases, the resettlement agency shall
pay the affected household compensation not only for the house demolished but also the house
site taken.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 R4 - AUGUST 2004                       PAGE 121



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
(1) For those who choose to build their own houses, the local government shall provide free of
charge house sites at the space rate of 3Om2 per person. The demolisher is responsible for
smoothing the ground and providing water and power supplies to the affected households. The
resettled persons may choose to build multi-story houses with the ground floor used as a shop
for business. It is known through survey that the resettled persons can perfectly build houses of
the same area as their former houses in the resettlement area with the compensation money
received.
(2) The resettled persons may choose to buy resettlement houses provided by the government at
a reduced price. They may buy such houses at the price equivalent to the compensation and at
the space standard of 1 8m2 per person. For limitation of design, the excessive space is to be
purchased at a rate 50% as much as the combination price (construction cost and land price
included), if it is not more than 5m2 and if the space is in excess of Sm2 but less than the space
of the former house demolished, it is may be purchased at the combination price. Any part
exceeding the space of the former house demolished is to be purchased at the price of
commercial houses. The demolisher is responsible for smoothing the ground and providing
water, power and gas supplies to the affected households.
(3) For families who are not willing to purchase houses provided at a preferential price or built their
own houses on sites provided free, they might use the compensation money received to
purchase commercial houses in the city. As the project-executing agency pays the house site
compensation at the space rate of 3Om2 per person at the price of RMB300/m2, this
compensation enables them to buy second-hand houses in Changshou District. Many of the
second-hand house buildings in Changshou District are houses left by enterprises and
institutions. They are relatively convenient in location and good in structure. Furthermore, those
who choose to get resettled by monetary compensation and purchase commercial houses in
Changshou District will be exempted from all the purchase fees and taxes. See TABLE 6-16 for
information about the supply of new commercial houses and second-hand houses.

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
The uniform resettlement houses (the layout types are among 80-120m ) and resettlement area are
located in the new urban area of Taohua Township and complete with various supplementary
facilities and well-developed transport and communication systems. Taohua New City is the future
political centre of Changshou District, as all the major district government agencies will be moved
here. A number of public facilities have been planed, which include administrative offices,
apartments, commercial and financial establishments, entertainment, medical and sanitation
institutions, green spaces and other urban infrastructures. As the area is located at the joint of the
Chongqing-Fuling and Chongqing-Wanzhou expressways, urbanization of the area has been in
fast development since these expressways were opened to traffic. According to the schedule, the
area will reach its planed size in 3 to 5 years. The Taohua New City Area covers an area of 6.7 km2
with a planed population of nearly 100,000 million. Since the existing old city area is too small and
too densely populated, 30,000 residents will be moved to the new city area and so will be the
district government agencies, institutions and functionaries and a number of schools will be built
there, all of which will bring about 20,000 people this area. Further, the construction of chemical
industrial park and special product Industrial park will enlarge the area to 36km2. As the design of
both parks does not include the residential area, about 20,000 people will go to reside in the
Taohua New City area. With the quickening of the urbanization process, it is estimated that 6,000
people will go to reside in the new city area each year. This means an increase of 30,000 people in
5 years. The city plan requires that the new city area will take shape in 3 years and completed in 5
years with a total population of 99.100.
The newly built houses are better in structure and quality and the resettled residents will feel more
convenient in daily life, work and their children's schooling than before. Their living standard and
quality of life will be much improved. The field survey shows that more than 90% of them prefer to
build their own houses.
6.4.4 RESETTLEMENT OF ENTERPRISES
The project will affect three enterprises by land acquisition and 14.5 mu of land will be acquired.
Since the land to be acquired is left unused, land acquisition will not affect the operation of the
enterprises. They can get the compensation for loss of land only at the rate of RMB200,000/mu.
The price is subject to change according to the actual assessment when the compensation is
made.

6.5 BICHENG WATER SUPPLY PROJECT IN BISHAN COUNTY
The project will acquire 37.01 mu of land for permanent use and occupy 40.7 mu of land for
temporary use, affecting 296 people in 91 households including 54 labourers.
6.5.1 REHABILITATION OF PERMANENT LAND ACQUISITION

mu of wasteland, affecting 210 people in three groups of Huangjiao and Wuli Villages in Binan
Township and 54 people need to be resettled by production: The Qiancengyan water supply plant

station will acquire 9.21 mu of land including 8.35 mu of farmland and 0.86 mu of wasteland,

It is found from the survey that the land acquired is sloppy, difficult to toil and poor in yield and
none of the farmers are willing to cultivate. In addition, the agricultural output value of the two
villages account for about 1/4 of the total turnover. The income from farming, which is 12.7%, of a
rural family constitutes only a small part of its total income but the income from working in the
urban area accounts for a lion's share, which is 87.3%. Therefore, the impact caused by land
acquisition on the two villages will be quite limited.
6.5.1.2   REHABILITATION OF INCOME
(1) Resettlement plan
Currently there are many job opportunities for farmers in Bishan County. Young labouring people
are now seldom engaged in farming but instead go to work and run business in the city. Through
analysis of the scale of economic development, features of the agro-economic structure, per-capita
ownership of land resources and composition of the villagers' income and repeated hearing of the
comments of the villagers' representatives, it is agreed that the villagers affected by land
acquisition will be resettled in the following manners:
(1) Changing status
The affected farmers may choose to have their status changed and receive a total amount of
RMB16,000 as land compensation and resettlement subsidy. The village leadership will reallocate
land among villagers.
.For those who can have their status changed but are unwilling to do so, the village committee will
reallocate land among the villagers, that is, to allocate farmland give up by villagers not affected by
land acquisition but are willing to have their status changed to the former and the latter will have
their status changed and receive the land compensation and resettlement subsidy.
(2) Monetary compensation
For those affected farmers who are willing to remain in the rural area to contact land for farming
rather than having their status changed, the project-executing agency will make compensation
according to the space of land taken.
The two affected villages may receive a total amount of RMB1.408 million as land compensation
and resettlement subsidy, including RMBO.205 million for community 3 and RMBO.922 million for
community 5 of Huangjiao Village and RMBO.2805 million for Wuli Village.
Each mu of land taken can be compensated for RMB31,943-42,500. Based on the current deposit
interest rate 2.79% above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%, the real deposit rate is
2.232%. If the affected deposit the compensation RMB31,943-42,500 in the bank for 50 years,
they will get about RMB1,061-1,284 each year, which is more than their current yearly net income
RMB650 from cultivated land.
(3) Livelihood support
The status-changed persons may enjoy the basic endowment insurance and minimum subsistence
allowance for urban residents. Those who have secured basic endowment insurance and have
actually paid the premium for 15 years and longer may receive endowment insurance money on a
monthly basis after they have reached the age of 60 years (for men) and 55 years (for women). In
Bishan County, the minimum subsistence allowance is paid RMB145/month, which is more than
their average annual income of RMB600 from farming.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS- 23500321.R4 - AUGUST 2004                    PAGE 125



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
For those villagers who have chosen to get resettled by receiving monetary compensation and
whose families include surplus labourers, the village committee will provide them with training on
agricultural production technology and help them restructure their farming business to improve
income, such as developing greenhouse vegetable planting using the advantage of being close to
the urban area.
The local government will establish a complete labour service system to provide assistance to the
affected villagers such as providing them with information on employment, vocational training,
consultation with the local enterprises, etc. to pave the way for them to get employed.
In the past 20 years, township enterprises and private businesses have experienced a fast growth,
which have accounted for more than 90% of the county's industrial sector and become the major
part of the local economy. Machine building, building materials and shoe making have become
three mainstay industries in Bishan County. Large enterprises such as Bishan Anzi Cement Mill
and Chongqing Dajiang Motorcycle Engines Co. Ltd. have come into being. In Bicheng Township,
there are Aokang Shoe-making Co., Chuandong Shock Absorbers Factory, Shudong Machinery
Plant, Shazhichuan Leather Shoe Factory, Bluelight Motorcycle and Car Parts Factory,
Qiangrenzhou Leather Shoes Factory, Kerse Leather Shoes Factory, Zongshen Three-wheel
Motorcycles Co. and Bicheng Knitting Mill. The ordinary workers in these enterprises receive a
salary of RMB600-1,200. The township and enterprises and private businesses in Bicheng
Township provide 3,000-4,000 jobs each year, including cleaners, cargadors and construction
workers. According to the survey, the average monthly salary of the ordinary workers in the local
enterprise is about RMB500-600. By acquisition such measures, the farmers' income will increase
as the enterprises keep growing so that it will not be lower than it was before land acquisition or
even higher.
6.5.2 REHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
The temporary land occupation for this project is caused by the construction of water supply
pipelines. This will affect two villages and 40.73 mu of land will be temporarily occupied. The
occupation of land will last for not yet three months (but will be regarded as three months when
making compensation). According to the rates of compensation for loss of crops during temporary
occupation of land, the compensation will be RMB1, 200/mu for farmland and RMB1, 400/mu for
fishpond. As the loss of crops and fishes during one quarter is about RMB500/mu and RMB800/mu
respectively, the compensation is much higher than the actual loss of farmland and fishpond.
The temporarily occupied land will be restored after use by the constructor. As the operation on the
temporarily occupied land includes trench cutting, pipe laying and backfilling, the constructor will
restore the land by cutting and backfilling the ground section by section according to the actual
condition. Each section will be restored in no longer than 2 months. By this method, the impact
caused by temporary occupation of land will be reduced to a minimum.
In one word, after getting the compensation, the affected villagers' livelihood will not deteriorate but
instead will recover to the level before land taking.
6.5.3 REHABILITATION OF AFFECTED VULNERABLE GROUPS
The vulnerable groups to be affected by this project are old people's families in Huangjiao village.
Their conditions are as follows:
Zhang Guangming, aged 97, lives in Huangjiao Village. There are 12 members in his family with a
total space of farmland of 1.4 mu, of which o.65 mu will be occupied permanently for constructing
the water plant. The annual income of the family is RMB14, 720 mainly eared by his children from
working away from home. The income from farming accounts for only a very small part in the total
income. Therefore land acquisition will produce no major impact on the financial standing of their
families.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AUGUST 2004                    PAGE 126



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Zhu Yuqing, 84 years of age, lives in Huangjiao Village. The family consists of the old couple only
without any children and has a space of farmland of 0.7 mu, of which 0.3 mu will be occupied
permanently for constructing the water plant. The annual income of the family is RMB4, 000 and
farming is the major source of income.
There are three altematives to resettle these disadvantaged people:
Alternative 1: Change status and leave them in the family. The project owner pays the land
compensation and resettlement subsidy to them (or their children) through the village leadership so
that they spend the rest of their life in the family. Their children bear all the cost of supporting them
and at the same time they enjoy all the welfare given to the urban residents.
Alternative 2: Reallocate the land. If the old person (or his children looking after him/her) wishes to
get farmland, the village leadership will coordinate and uses their chance of status change to get
the farmland of other people in the village who are not affected by land acquisition but wish to
change status. In this way they will get the farmland they want. By land reallocation within a narrow
scope, the old people's families can get more farmland and by providing them with technical
training and assistance to restructure their farming, their livelihood can recover to the level before
land acquisition.
Alternative 3: Resettle by public welfare. The land compensation and resettlement subsidy for
these people are paid to the local public welfare bureau. In this way Zhu and his wife can pay
regular visit to the public welfare bureau to get their subsistence money. Or the land compensation
and resettlement subsidy are paid to the neighbourhood rest home in Bicheng Township where the
old couple will be acquired care of for the rest of their life.
Moreover, during construction of the water plant, priority will be given to employing the children of
the vulnerable group to do some work of low technical requirement such as ground smoothing,
excavation and soil removal on the construction site so that they can get some income.
Following the custom of respecting and caring about the old in Longshui Township, the government
will pay visit to the affected people's homes in all major traditional holidays. Through such visits,
the government is able to know how this vulnerable group are living and find out the problems they
have in daily life and feed back the information to the project owner and independent supervisor.
The project owner will then come up with solutions according to the actual situation.
6.5.4 AFFECTED GROUND ATTACHMENTS
The affected ground attachments will be compensated for by the project-executing agency and
rebuilt by the farmers.

acquisition, the per-capita space of farmland will diminish by 0.64 mu, down by 12.3%. If the
average annual yield of the farmland is RMB500 per mu, the per-capita income from farmland will
go down by RMB61. As the net annual per-capita income of the village was RMB3, 022, it will go
down by 5% after land acquisition.
Apparently, land acquisition will create no significant impact on any of these villages.
6.6.1.2    REHABILITATION OF INCOME
(1) Resettlement plan
Through extensive consultations with the affected villagers, resettlement will be arranged for this
project in the following two ways:
( Changing status
As all the seven affected villages are located in the planned area for construction of the county
seat, the land will be acquired gradually in the coming years in the ongoing urbanization process.
Therefore, resettlement of the affected villagers may take the form of changing status depending
on the actual condition and villagers' willingness. The status-changed persons will receive a total
amount of RMB16,000 as land compensation and resettlement subsidy and their land will be
reallocated among villagers.
For those who can have their status changed but are unwilling to do so, the village committee will
reallocate land among the villagers, that is, to allocate farmland give up by villagers not affected by
land acquisition but are willing, to have their status changed to the former and the latter will have
their status changed and receive the land compensation and resettlement subsidy. The affected
.farmers may choose to have their status changed and receive a total amount of RMB16,000 as
land compensation and resettlement subsidy. The village leadership will reallocate land among
villagers.
SOGREAH CONSULTANTS - 23500321 .R4 - AuGusT 2004                          PAGE 128



CHONGQING MUNICIPALITY - THE WORLD BANK
CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
For those who can have their status changed but are unwilling to do so, the village committee will
reallocate land among the villagers, that is, to allocate farmland give up by villagers not affected by
land acquisition but are willing to have their status changed to the former and the latter will have
their status changed and receive the land compensation and resettlement subsidy.
( Monetary compensation
For those affected farmers who are willing to remain in the rural area to contact land for farming
rather than having their status changed, the project-executing agency will make compensation
according to the space of land taken. Each mu of land taken can be compensated for RMB34,850.
Based on the current deposit interest rate 2.79% above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%,
the real deposit rate is 2.232%. If the affected deposit the compensation RMB34,850 in the bank
for 50 years, they will get about RMB1,158 each year, which is much more than their current yearly
net income RMB500 from cultivated land.
The seven affected villages will get a total amount of RMB1 1.895 million as land compensation and
resettlement subsidy.
Q) Livelihood support
The status-changed persons may enjoy the basic endowment insurance and minimum subsistence
allowance for urban residents. Those who have secured basic endowment insurance and have
actually paid the premium for 15 years and longer may receive endowment insurance money on a
monthly basis after they have reached the age of 60 years (for men) and 55 years (for women). In
Bishan County, the minimum subsistence allowance is paid RMB1451month, which is more than
their average annual income of RMB600 from farming.
For those villagers who have chosen to get resettled by receiving monetary compensation and
whose families include surplus labourers, the village committee will provide them with training on
agricultural production technology, and help them restructure their farming business to improve
income, such as developing greenhouse vegetable planting using the advantage of being close to
the urban area.
The local government will establish a complete labour service system to provide assistance to the
affected villagers such as providing them with information on employment, vocational training,
consultation with the local enterprises, etc. to pave the way for them to get employed.
In the past 20 years, township enterprises and private businesses have experienced a fast growth,
which have accounted for more than 90% of the county's industrial sector and become the major
part of the local economy. Machine building, building materials and shoe making have become
three mainstay industries in Bishan County. Large enterprises such as Bishan Anzi Cement Mill
and Chongqing Dajiang Motorcycle Engines Co. Ltd. have come into being. In Bicheng Township,
there are Aokang Shoe-making Co., Chuandong Shock Absorbers Factory, Shudong Machinery
Plant, Shazhichuan Leather Shoe Factory, Bluelight Motorcycle and Car Parts Factory,
Qiangrenzhou Leather Shoes Factory, Kerse Leather Shoes Factory, Zongshen Three-wheel
Motorcycles Co. and Bicheng Knitting Mill. The ordinary workers in these enterprises receive a
salary of RMB600-1,200. The township and enterprises and private businesses in Bicheng
Township provide 3,000-4,000 jobs each year, including cleaners, cargadors and construction
workers. According to the survey, the average monthly salary of the ordinary workers in the local
enterprise is about RMB500-600. By acquisition such measures, the farmers' income will increase
as the enterprises keep growing so that it will not be lower than it was before land acquisition or
even higher.

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
At present, the ongoing urban construction and enterprises now in operation and those under
construction in the development zones may provide a great number of job opportunities for the
affected people (See TABLE 6-20). It consists of the machine-building centre that integrates the
functions of development, production and sales and West-China Shoemaking Park that integrates
the functions of shoemaking, technical information provision, and technical training and product
distribution.
The Park Area covers a total space of 11.4 km2 of which 1.4 km2 is used as the start-up zone, 1.98
km2 as the expansion zone and the rest as far-future planning zone. The planned target of this park
area is to finish constructing 6 km2 of it within 5 years (from 2003 to 2007) to introduce 120
enterprises that produces high value-added products and are relatively large in size. The total
investment of these enterprises will amount up to RMB4 billion with an annual output value of over
RMB15 billion. In five years time, these enterprises are expected to generate a total tax revenue of
RMB1.2 billion, or at least RMBO.4 billion by 2007 and employ 70,000 people.
Currently, altogether 22 industrial enterprises have been introduced into this park area, covering a
total space of 2,417.26 mu, of which 406,000 m2 of houses have been constructed with a total
construction investment of RMB81.574 million. The designed total output value of the completed
space is RMB4.79591 billion, meaning every square kilometre of the area will generate a yield of
RMB2.97883 billion. Up to the end of November 2003, the park has turned out an output of
RMBI1.79623 billion and tax revenue of RMB52.11 million, employing more than 6,000 people. So
far, construction of the 1.4 km2 start-up area has finished and 19 enterprises has moved into it,
including 8 that have been in operation such as JINGUAN AUTOS and HONGYU PRECISION
MACHINES, 4 that will get into operation such as the ZONGZAO THREE WHEELERS and 7 that
are under construction such as the SHUANGXING GROUP.

6.6.2 RESTORATIONREHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
The temporary occupation of land for this project involves 26 mu of land Crop compensation for
land temporarily occupied will be paid in such as manner that the loss in one year of occupation will
be compensated for as 2.5 quarters, which means a total sum of compensation money of
RMB2,500. Constructing the project will occupy the land for about one year and the compensation
obtained is much higher than the actual loss as the average annual output value of the farmland is
only RMB1, 200 per mu. Therefore, the farmers' livelihood will not be affected.
After the project is completed, the affected choose how to restore the land. The constructor re-
cultivates the farmland occupied and returns it to the affected; village and group organize to check
and accept.

6.6.3 RESETTLEMENT OF RURAL RESIDENTS
Altogether 4,193.49 m2 of rural residential houses will be demolished for constructing this project.
The resettled residents will be resettled by monetary compensation (the standard being
RMB270/m2 for brick+concrete structure houses, RMB220/m2 for brick+wood structure houses,
RMB150/m2 for earth+wood structure houses, and RMB60 for simple structure houses). The
affected people receiving the compensation money have three alternatives to make, namely, to
construct their own houses, purchase cheap resettlement houses, and purchase commercial
houses. In the former case, the resettlement agency shall pay compensation to the owner of the
house demolished and at the same time provide him free of charge with a house site. In the latter
two cases, the resettlement agency shall pay the affected household compensation not only for the
house demolished but also the house site taken.
(1) For those who choose to build their own houses, the local government shall provide free of
charge house sites at the space rate of 3Dm2 per person. The demolisher is responsible for
smoothing the ground and providing water and power supplies to the affected households. The
resettled persons may choose to build multi-story houses with the ground floor used as a shop
for business. It is known through survey that the resettled persons can perfectly build houses of
the same area as their former houses in the resettlement area with the compensation money
received.
(2) The resettled persons may choose to buy resettlement houses provided by the government at
a reduced price. They may buy such houses at the price equivalent to the compensation and at
the space standard of 18m2 per person. For limitation of design, the excessive space is to be
purchased at a rate 50% as much as the he combination price (construction cost and land price
included) if it is not more than 5m2 and if the space is in excess of 5m2 but less than the space
of the former house demolished, it is may be purchased at the combination price. Any part
exceeding the space of the former house demolished is to be purchased at the price of
commercial houses. The demolisher is responsible for smoothing the ground and providing
water, power and gas supplies to the affected households.
(3) For families who are not willing to purchase houses provided at a preferential price or built their
own houses on sites provided free, they might use the compensation money received to
purchase commercial houses in the city. As they will be compensated for house sites at the
space rate of 3Dm2 per person at the price of RMB300/m2, the compensation enables them to
buy new or second-hand houses in Bishan County seat.
(4) Those who purchase commercial houses in Tongliang County will be exempted from all the
purchase fees and taxes. See TABLE 6.22 for information about the supply of new commercial
houses and second-hand houses in Bishan County. Many of the second-hand house buildings
in Bishan County are houses left by enterprises and institutions. They are relatively convenient
in location and good in quality and structure. Furthermore, those who choose to get resettled
by monetary compensation and purchase commercial houses in Bishan County will be
exempted from all the purchase fees and taxes. See TABLE 6-21 for information about the
supply of new commercial houses and second-hand houses.

According to the general plan of Chongqing municipality, Bicheng Township will be the traffic gate

quality of life will be much improved. Through discussions with the affected rural residents, more

This project will affect 101 people in 8 enterprises.

dormitory buildings will be demolished will rebuild them on a new location near the original site and
reconstruction will be arranged during the vacation to minimize causing impact on the normal
operation of the college. In either case, the land price for these enterprises will be compensated for
at the evaluated actual price.
The enterprises or institutions whose enclosure wall and pump house are demolished may use the
compensation to rebuild them.

6.6.5    REHABILITATION OF AFFECTED INFRASTRUCTURES AND GROUND ATTACHMENTS
The affected infrastructures and ground attachments will be recovered and reconstructed their
respective owners with the compensation money paid to them by the project owner. Special
facilities will be restored in such a way that the existing ones will not be demolished until the new
ones are built in other places to void affecting the livelihood and business operation of the
residents, enterprises, institutions and shops around the project area.

The project will acquire 395.75 mu of land for permanent use and 30 mu of land for temporary use,
affecting 12 people in 4 rural households, 6 people in 1 urban household, 28 people in 3

6.7.1.1     ANALYSIS OF IMPACT

Changtou River improvement component.will acquire 20 mu of land including 9 mu of collectively
owned farmland, 8 mu of wasteland and 3 mu of riverside shallow land.

From TABLE 6-24, it can be seen that this project has no significant impact on the four villages
because only a small percentage of farmland will be acquired. Of the four villages, Zitong Village is
affected most. Altogether 64.5 mu of land is acquired; accounting for 15% of the total space, and
159 persons are affected of whom 143 need to be resettled by production. The per-capita space of
farmland is 0.38 mu after acquisition, down by 1 .6%. The average annual yield of farmland in the
village is RMB500 per mu and land acquisition will reduce this figure by RMB8. As the per-capita
net income of the village was RMB2, 356, Apparently, the project has no significant impact on the
four villages by land acquisition and just as the land acquired accounts for only a small part of the
total area of farmland, the impact of land acquisition on the farmer's income is thus quite limited.
According to the survey, all the farmland to be acquired is within the flood-affected area and thus
either seeding or harvesting will be significantly affected each year. After the embankment is
completed, part of the farmland originally affected by flood but not acquired will have a better yield.
Therefore land acquisition of the project has no significant impact on the local residents.
6.7.1.2   REHABILITATION OF INCOME
1.   Resettlement plan
As all the four affected villages are located in the planned area for construction of the county seat,
the land will be acquired gradually in the coming 5-10 years during the ongoing urbanization
process. Therefore, resettlement of the affected villagers may take the form of changing status
depending on the actual condition and villagers' willingness. The status-changed persons will
receive a total amount of RMB16,000 as land compensation and resettlement subsidy.
2.    Monetary compensation
For those affected farmers who are willing to remain in the rural area to contact land for farming
rather than having their status changed, the project-executing agency will make compensation
according to the space of land taken. Each mu of land taken can be compensated for RMB45,000.
Based on the current deposit interest rate 2.79% above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%,
the real deposit rate is 2.232%. If the affected deposit the compensation RMB34,850 in the bank
for 50 years, they will get about RMB1,497 each year, which is much more than their current yearly
net income RMB600 from cultivated land.
The four affected villages will get a total amount of RMB8.913 million as land compensation and
resettlement subsidy.
3.   Livelihood support
The status-changed persons may enjoy the basic endowment insurance and minimum subsistence
allowance for urban residents. Those who have secured basic endowment insurance and have
actually paid the premium for 15 years and longer may receive endowment insurance money on a
monthly basis after they have reached the age of 60 years (for men) and 55 years (for women). In
Bishan County, the minimum subsistence allowance is paid at the rate of RMB145/month.
For those villagers who have chosen to get resettled by receiving monetary compensation and
whose families include surplus labourers, the village committee will provide them with training on
agricultural production technology and help them restructure their farming business to improve
income, such as developing greenhouse vegetable planting using the advantage of being close to
the urban area.

CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
The local government will establish a complete labour service system to provide assistance to the
affected villagers such as providing them with information on employment, vocational training,
consultation with the local enterprises, etc. to pave the way for them to get employed.
According to a survey of the income level of status-changed persons in Wulong County in the past
three years, the average annual income of those engaged in the secondary and tertiary industries
in the city will be about RMB5,000 to 6,000 by 2005, which is much higher than it used to be
before resettlement.
6.7.2 REHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
Temporary land acquisition will affect three villages. Altogether 30 mu of land will be acquired for
temporary use, including 17 mu of collectively owned land. The temporary occupation of farmland
will necessitate the compensation for loss of crops. As the farmland will be acquired for one year
and two growing seasons will be affected which will be compensated for as 2.5 seasons, each mu
of farmland may receive a crop compensation of RMB2,500. If calculated in terms of the annual
yield of farmland in one year, the temporary occupation of land will bring about a loss of RMB1,500
per mu. The compensation is thus more than the actual loss of the farmland. This means that the
villagers' livelihood will not be affected.
The temporarily acquired land will be restored and returned to the village by the constructor.
6.7.3 RESETTLEMENT OF URBAN RESIDENTS
This project will involve the demolition of 1,450m2 of residential houses including 380m2 of urban
residences and 1,070m2 of rural residences, affecting 18 persons in 5 households. The urban
resettled persons may receive monetary compensation at the rate of RMB450/m2 (land prices
included)for brick+concrete structure houses, and the rural resettled persons may receive
RMB270/m2 for brick+concrete structure houses (including land price). They may, at their option,
purchase houses in the urban area at a reduced price.
Those who purchase commercial houses in Wulong County seat will benefit from a preferential
policy that allows them to buy a space of 18m2 per person at the compensation price. For limitation
of design, the excessive space is to be purchased at a rate 50% as much as the combination
cost(construction cost and land prices included)if it is not more than 5m2 and if the space is in
excess of 5m2 but less than the space of the former house demolished, it is may be purchased at
the combination price. Any part exceeding the space of the former house demolished is to be
purchased at the price of commercial houses.
Those who are not willing to purchase cheap resettlement houses may use their compensation to
buy commercial or second-hand houses in the urban area. See TABLE 6-25 for information about
the supply of houses for resettlement.
There is only one urban residence to be resettled. The owner of the residence has another house
and the residence in question is currently being rented by other people. The tenant of the residence
will be offered, 3 months before demolishing the house, information about the vacancy of houses
and help in finding the house and during movement. The owner of the house will be paid of
monetary compensation for the house as well as for the loss of rent for a period of 6 month at the
rate of RMB300 per month. Compensation will also be made for the damage of telephone line,
cable TV and other facilities and allowances for movement, transition and installation of water and
power supplies will be provided. As this family has a residence in the urban area, they may use this
sum of compensation money to continue doing business or purchase houses in the urban area to
let out.

6.7.4 RESETTLEMENT OF RURAL RESIDENTS
For constructing this project, four rural residential houses will be demolished. The displace persons
may receive compensation at the rate of RMB270/m2 for brick+concrete structure houses and
RMB180/m2 for earth+wood structure houses.
The Changtu River improvement component will affect one family, whose land will be acquired and
house demolished. The family includes two adults and one child. They make a living by doing small
business in a rented shop in the urban area. Currently their income comes mainly from business
and has little reliance on land. As the project-executing agency will pay them compensation for
house site at the space rate of 3Om3 per person at the price of RMB150/m2, the compensation they
receive will enable them to buy new or second-hand houses in the city. So after moving into the
city, their living standard will not degrade and their work, livelihood and their child's schooling will
become even more convenient. The other three families will not be affected by land acquisition.
Except the one to be demolished, Chen Honglin's family has another house measuring about
500m2 in floor space nearby. Though consultation, the family is willing to get resettlement by
monetary compensation. Chen Jianming's family includes two adults and one child and they
currently make a living by working for others. Through consultation, they are willing to get resettled
by monetary compensation. With this sum of money they can purchase a new or second-hand
house in the city at a cheap price. Tan Chunpo's family consists of four members. The family
makes a living by working for others. After their house is demolished, they are willing to get
resettled by receiving monetary compensation. Similarly, they can use this sum of money to
purchase a new or second-hand house in the urban area. As this family has difficulty getting
employed in the city, they will be provided with assistance such as giving free technical training to
the two labourers in the family so that they can find jobs in the city. In this way their living standard
can be restored to at least the former level.
From TABLE 6-25, it can be seen that the residential centres now being developed in Wulong
County seat can provide houses of various spaces and internal structure types. These residential
centres are normally complete with facilities and convenient transport system. There are also an
ample supply of second-hand houses in the city, most of which are house buildings of local law
courts, banks, power supply company, Xinhua book store and other institutions. These houses are
still good in quality and structure and are located in areas with convenient transportation. They are
available in different internal structures for the resettled persons to choose from. Therefore, after
moving into the city, the resettled residents will expect a considerable improvement in living
standard and quality.

6.7.5 RESETTLEMENT OF ENTERPRISES
The project will affect three enterprises with 2,045 m2 of houses to be demolished.
See TABLE 6-26 for the resettlement of the affected enterprises. After receiving the monetary
compensation, the enterprises may decide whether or not to reconstruct their houses. The concrete
slab yard has not been in operation for years and reconstruction is out of the question. The tobacco
re-drying plant may use the compensation fund to renovate the existing empty houses into
dormitory for the migrant workers and therefore reconstruction is unnecessary. The material
recovery company may use the compensation fund to rebuild houses on another site provided free
by the planning department of the local government. These enterprises will get compensation for
economic losses caused by resettlement because they will receive compensation not only for the
loss of houses but also for the loss of land. Resettlement of the material recovery company in
another place will be arranged as early as possible to enable early reconstruction and
rehabilitation.

6.7.6 RESETTLEMENT OF SHOPS
The project will affect 12 persons in 2 shops. They will receive a compensation of RMB45,000.
Both shops are run on rent. Since the construction of the project will cause the shops to temporarily
stop operation, the demolisher will, three months before construction of the project, provide the
renters with other houses including shops in similar location and at similar rate of rent and help
them find the houses and arrange operation. Moreover, the owner of the two shops will be paid
compensation for rent losses of one year at the rate of RMB20, 000. The duration of compensation
is 10 months in principle but may be adjusted according to the actual time of impact.

* construction so as not to affect their business operation and should pay them movement allowance
at the rate of RMB1 5/mi.
6.7.7 REHABILITATION OF VULNERABLE GROUPS
The project office has also surveyed the vulnerable groups to be affected by the project. while
conducting the socio-economic survey (See next Table). This project will affect 11 families of the
vulnerable group, which include 4 families having handicapped person(s), 2 families consisting
mainly of women and 5 families consisting of old people living alone. All of these families will be
affected by land acquisition. Their source of income includes rental money earned from alienating
or letting out collectively owned land paid to each family member and the compensation paid by the
township government and village leadership. The total sum of the two amounts is about
RMB200/month. From the finding of the survey, it can be seen that the land to be acquired by the
project from the vulnerable group is not significant in space and, since the farmland in the land-
acquisition area will be flooded each year and original yield of the farmland is already subject to the
impact of flood, land acquisition actually has no major impact on the income of the affected people.

'The affected infrastructure and ground attachments will be restored by their respective owners after
being compensated for by the project owner. Of these facilities, the cell phone relay tower, high
and low voltage power lines and other special faculties will be built in other locations before
demolishing the existing ones so as not to affect the livelihood of the residents and operation of the
enterprises, institutions, and shops nearby.
6.8 PROJECT IN JIANGJIN CITY
The project will acquire 12.36 mu of land for permanent use and 101.71 mu for temporary use,
affecting 279 people in 79 households and 19 people need to be resettled by production.
6.8.1 REHABILITATION OF PERMANENTLY LAND ACQUISITION
6.8.1.1    ANALYSIS OF IMPACT
This project will acquire 12.36 mu of land for permanent use, affecting 126 persons in 39
households in 4 villages. As the total space of land to be acquired is relatively small with the per-
capital space of land decreasing only by 0.001 mu, land acquisition will have no significant impact
on the villagers (See TABLE 6-28).

family has a total space of farmland of 3.68 mu with a monthly income of RMB1,500. The male
labourers of the family often go out to work as migrant workers and get a relatively stable income
annually. The female labourers stay at home farming. There is still a space of 2.48 mu of farmland
left after acquisition. As the yield of land in the area is poor, they are willing to get resettled by
receiving monetary compensation rather than reallocation of land. Yuan Zhongwen's family in
Taping Village receives the least impact of land acquisition with only 0.03 mu of land acquired. The
four-member family has a total space of farmland of 1.85 mu with a monthly income of RMB1,200.
'Land acquisition will produce no impact on their living standard.

CHONGQING URBAN ENVIRONMENT PROJECT
RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
Also according to the survey, a majority of villagers in these two villages are working locally or
elsewhere as migrant workers. Land acquisition actually has no practical impact on their income.
6.8.1.2   REHABILITATION OF INCOME
1    Resettlement plan
Unsatisfied with the low yield of farmland, the villagers affected by permanent land acquisition are
unwilling to get resettled by relocation of land. A consensus has been reached through consultation
that they will be resettled by receiving monetary compensation. According to the rates of
compensation, the two villages will get a total amount of RMB310,000 as land compensation and
resettlement subsidy. At the consent of a majority of 2/3 of the affected villagers, the land
compensation and resettlement subsidy will be paid to the affected labourers according to the
space of land acquired. Thus, each of the affected labourers can get a total of RMB16,379 with the
land compensation and resettlement subsidy putting together.
Each mu can be compensated RMB 25,184. Based on the current deposit interest rate 2.79%
above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%, the real deposit rate is 2.232%. If the affected
deposit the compensation RMB25, 184 in the bank for 50 years, they will get about RMB837 each
year, which is more than their current yearly net income RMB492 from cultivated land.
After receiving the compensation money, they may grow cash crops on the remaining space of
farmland and enlarge the scale of animal husbandry. Therefore, it is quite possible that their
livelihood can be restored to the former level.
2.    Livelihood support
The following arrangements will be made to resettle the labourers in the affected villages:
(1) The local government agencies will discuss with the nearby enterprises to persuade them to
give priority to employing the affected villagers. There are seyeral major enterprises in the
affected area such as Tiantian Printing Co. Ltd. which generates an annual output of RMB10
million, Jingu Xinxing Machinery Plant, which runs import and output business in container
connecting bolts, and a liquor production and sales base. Now the Shuangfu Industrial Park
Area is acquisition shape, where 25 enterprises has moved in, introducing a total investment of
RMB430 million. Of these enterprises, Chongqing Meike Motor Technology Co. Ltd. with a total
investment of RMB200 million is now clearing the site for constructing its houses, Chongqing
Ruili Machine Manufacturing Co. Ltd. has already been in operation, Chongqing Changgu
Industrial & Trading Co. is now constructing its workshops, etc. After the water supply project is
completed, more and more enterprises will be attracted into the industrial park area.
Doubtlessly this will promote employment in the project area. The affected local villagers may
take part in the construction of these enterprises. Unskilled villagers will be provided with
vocational training. It is found from the survey that the average income level of the ordinary
workers in the local enterprises is within RMB500-600. As the enterprises grow in business,
the farmers working in these enterprises can expect a growth in income.
(2) With the execution of the water supply project, the constructor will give priority to employing the
local labourers to take part in the civil works. As most of the villagers have worked in
construction companies as masons, carriers, reinforcement bar binders, they are highly
experienced in doing such specialized jobs.
(3) A monitoring mechanism will be established to ensure that the resettled persons get properly
resettled and compensated so that their production and livelihood will not be lower than the
level before resettlement.

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
6.8.2 REHABILITATION OF TEMPORARY LAND OCCUPATION
The project will take 101.7 mu of land for temporary use, affecting 10 villages in one township.
Through consultation with the local villagers, it is agreed that compensation for temporary
occupation of land will be made in such as way that the loss of yield in one farming season will be
compensated for as if it were in two farming seasons at the rate of RMB900 per mu for loss of
crops and RMB1, 200 for loss of fishes. Since the land temporarily acquired will undergone
operations such as trench excavation, pipe laying and backfilling, it is known that the constructor
will carry out the excavating and backfilling operations section by section along the alignment and
each section of land will be restored in no longer than one month. This arrangement will reduce the
impact of temporary occupation of land to a minimum. To sum up, after receiving compensation,
the livelihood of the residents in the villages will not be adversely affected and can even restore to
the level before land acquisition.
6.8.3 REHABILITATION OF VULNERABLE GROUPS
The project will affect four handicapped people in four families located respectively in Halloo,
Gaohu and Guanghua Villages. According to the survey, Chen Jiezhong's family in Hailuo Village
has 1.41 mu of farmland of which 0.3 mu will be permanently acquired and family's average
monthly income is RMB800. Song Jieren's family in Gaohu Village has 1.9 mu of farmland of which
0.2 mu will be permanently acquired and the family's average monthly income is RMB500. Li Jun's
family in Hailuo Village has 2 mu of farmland of which 0.1 mu will be temporarily acquired and the
family's average monthly income is RMB1,000. Wang Zhouliang's family in Guanghua Village has
1.1 mu of farmland of which 0.4 mu will be temporarily acquired and the family's average monthly
income is RMB1,200. All of them have a stable income from working as migrant workers and only a
small part of their farmland will be acquired. Therefore land acquisition will virtually has little impact
on them. After being properly compensated, their livelihood will restore to the level before land
acquisition.
The two handicapped people's families affected by permanent land acquisition will not only receive
monetary compensation and resettlement subsidy but also be given priority in having the healthy
members of the families settled. For the other two handicapped people's families affected by
temporary occupation of land, the local govemment will consult the constructor to have their land
restored first and pay them the crop compensation. in time. As each of these families also includes
normal members, they will take case of the handicapped ones in the family. According to the
Official Document No. JCN(2003)173, these handicapped people will be exempted from the
agriculture tax, which will further relieve them of financial burden. After receiving the monetary
compensation duly paid to them, they can expect that their living standard will be restored to the
level before land acquisition.
Generally speaking, all measures possible will be acquired to help and support the impoverished
vulnerable group so that their livelihood is restored to the former level and gradually becomes well
off.
6.8.4 REHABILITATION OF INFRASTUCTURE AND GROUND ATTACHMENTS
The project will temporarily take 1,680 m2 of the section between Wenjiadian and Huangjiayuanzi
on the Jin-Ma highway route from July 1, 2004. According to the actual condition, the temporary
passageway will be constructed separately in half the width to avoid blocking the traffic.
Construction will begin five days after acquisition the land and be completed and traffic restored in
two days' time. Meanwhile, compensation will be paid to the highway management agency
according to Article IlIl: "Rates of compensation for Highway Assets in Chongqing" of Annex 1 of
Chongqing Municipal Communication Commission's Official Document No. YJW(2000)325.

RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN
The three power line poles affected by the Level II pressurizing pump station will be moved slightly
off the construction site. Thus before constructing the pump station, the switching off and on of
power will be so timed as to avoid the peak hours of power consumption by the local residents. Any
arrangement regarding the use of power will be duly announced to the local residents so as to
minimize the impact caused by switching off of power. After the power line poles are resettled,
construction of the pump station will have no impact on the local residents' livelihood as due to the
interruption of power supply.
For the 855 fruit trees affected by the project, their owners will be compensated at the rate of
RMB45 per piece according to the standard set.
6.9 PROJECT IN BEIBEI DISTRICT
The project will take 23.2 mu of land for permanently use and 8.1 mu of land for temporary use,
affecting 64 persons in 19 villages and 24 persons need to be reseKtled by production.
6.9.1 REHABILITATION OF PERMANENT LAND OCCUPATION
6.9.1.1   ANALYSIS OF IMPACT
The project will permanently take 23.2 mu of land including 19.9 mu of farmland and 3.3 mu of
state-owned land. Of the total space of land acquired, the water purification plant component will
take 17.8 mu and the high-elevation water tank component will take 2.1 mu. This will affect 50
people in two groups of two villages in Dongyang Township, Beibei District and 24 people need to
be resettled by production.

It is obvious that the project will take a small space of farmland and affect a small number of people
and families. This means each affected family still has sufficient farmland to cultivate. According to
the survey, the family affected most seriously by land acquisition has only 0.3 mu of farmland
acquired and they still have 0.8 mu left. The fact is that the major income of that family is from
secondary and tertiary industries and farming accounts for only an insignificant part of the total
income. As for other families, the land acquired accounts for even a smaller part of the total space.
It is known from the survey that since there are many non-agricultural job opportunities, very few
young labourers are engaged in farming and most of them work, run business or do other things in
the city. Obviously, as the major source of income of the affected labourers is the secondary and
tertiary industries, land acquisition will cause no significant impact on them in terms of income.
6.9.1.2    REHABILITATION OF INCOME
(1) Resettlement plan
Through discussions with Dongyang Township government, project owner, Jingtan Village
committee and affected villagers, it is agreed that all the farmers affected by land acquisition will be
resettled by receiving monetary compensation and the land compensation and resettlement
subsidy will be paid to the affected farmers.
The affected two villages can receive a total amount of RMB580,000 as land compensation and
resettlement subsidy. Each mu can be compensated RMB22,100-29,750. Based on the current
deposit interest rate 2.79% above 5 years, excluding tax on interest rate 20%, the real deposit rate
is 2.232%. If the affected deposit the compensation RMB22, 100-29,750 in the bank for 50 years,
they will get about RMB734-988 each year, which is more than their current yearly net income
RMB550 from cultivated land.
(2) Livelihood support
G As most of the villagers in the project area work, run business or do other things in the
city, the resettlement subsidy will be paid to the affected labourers themselves. This sum
of money will enable them to continue their present careers. The public welfare bureau will
employ technical personnel to train the surplus labourers and arrange them to work in the
nearby enterprises. The jobs available to them are mostly unskilled workers, security
guards, banisters, housekeepers, and cleaners with a wage level of RMB400-600 per
month. See next TABLE 6-30 for the basic facts about the candidate enterprises.

(I The village committee will use the land compensation to construct infrastructure,

Beibei Silkworm Breeding Farm has 800 mu of state-owned land. As there is no building to be
